## 19:1-6 — verses 1-6 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Tafsir of Surat Maryam (peace be upon her)

This is a Meccan surah.

Muhammad ibn Ishaq related in his Sira, from the hadith of Umm Salamah, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal related from Ibn Mas'ud, in the account of the migration from Mecca to the land of Abyssinia: that Ja'far ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, recited the opening of this surah before the Negus and his companions.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.

As for the discussion of the disconnected letters, it has already been given at the beginning of Surat al-Baqarah.

His saying, {A mention of the mercy of your Lord}, means: this is a mention of Allah's mercy upon His servant Zakariyya.

Yahya ibn Ya'mar read it as "He mentioned the mercy of your Lord to His servant Zakariyya."

Zakariyya can be read with a long or short final vowel, both being well known recitations. He was a great prophet among the prophets of the Children of Israel. In Sahih al-Bukhari it is recorded that he was a carpenter, meaning that he ate from the work of his own hands in carpentry.

His saying, {When he called upon his Lord with a hidden call}: some of the commentators said that he made his supplication hidden so that he would not be attributed with foolishness for seeking a child at his advanced age. This was related by al-Mawardi.

Others said he kept it hidden only because that is more beloved to Allah, as Qatadah said concerning this verse, {When he called upon his Lord with a hidden call}: Allah knows the pious heart and hears the hidden voice.

Some of the early generations said: he (peace be upon him) rose in the night, when his companions had gone to sleep, and began calling out to his Lord quietly, saying: "O my Lord, O my Lord, O my Lord," and Allah said: "Here I am, here I am, here I am."

{He said, "My Lord, indeed my bones have weakened within me"}, meaning: his strength had become feeble and had failed him, {and my head has flared up with grey hair}, meaning the grey had blazed through the black, as Ibn Duraid said in his Maqsurah:

"Do you not see my head, how its color resembles / a streak of dawn beneath the skirts of darkness,

And the white has flared up within the black, / like the flaring of fire in the embers of ghada wood."

The intent of this is to convey his weakness and old age, both its outward and inward signs.

His saying, {and I have never been unanswered by You, my Lord, in my prayer}, means: I have never known from You anything but acceptance in prayer; You have never once turned me away in what I asked of You.

His saying, {And indeed, I fear for my kinsmen after me}: most reciters read the ya of "al-mawali" with a fatha, making it the object. It is reported that al-Kisa'i made the ya quiescent, as the poet said:

"As though their hands upon the plain resembled the streaked ground, the hands of maidens passing silver coins to one another."

And another poet said:

"A young man such that, were he to rival the sun, it would cast off its veil, or the moon by night, it would cast down its reins."

And from this is the saying of Abu Tammam Habib ibn Aws al-Ta'i:

"The poetry within him grew jealous when I stayed awake for it, until I thought its verses would come to blows."

Mujahid, Qatadah, and al-Suddi said that by "al-mawali" he meant his paternal relatives ('asabah). Abu Salih said it meant "kalalah" (collateral relatives).

It is reported of the Commander of the Faithful, Uthman ibn Affan, may Allah be pleased with him, that he used to read it "wa inni khaffat al-mawali min wara'i" with a doubled fa, meaning: my kinsmen after me have become few.

According to the first reading, the reason for his fear was that he feared they would, after him, deal wrongly with the people, so he asked Allah for a son who would be a prophet after him, to guide them by his prophethood and what would be revealed to him. And he was answered in that. It was not that he feared their inheriting his wealth from him, for a prophet's rank is too great and his standing too exalted for him to be so concerned about his wealth, to the point of disdaining that his kinsmen inherit it, and asking instead for a son to take possession of the inheritance in place of them. This is one explanation.

The second: it is not mentioned that he possessed wealth; rather he was a carpenter who ate from the earnings of his own hands, and such a person does not amass wealth, especially not the prophets (peace be upon them), for they were the most ascetic of all people regarding this world.

The third: it is established in the two Sahihs, through more than one route, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "We are not inherited from; whatever we leave behind is charity." And in a report recorded by al-Tirmidhi with a sound chain: "We, the company of prophets, are not inherited from." Given this, his saying, {So grant me from Yourself an heir, who will inherit from me}, must be understood as referring to the inheritance of prophethood. This is why he said, {and inherit from the House of Ya'qub}, just as Allah Most High said, {And Sulayman inherited from Dawud} [al-Naml: 16], meaning in prophethood; for had it been a matter of wealth, he would not have been singled out from among his brothers for it, nor would there have been much benefit in reporting it, since it is a firmly established fact in all laws and religious communities that a child inherits from his father. So had it not been a special kind of inheritance, it would not have been mentioned. All of this is confirmed and established by what is authentically reported in the hadith: "We, the company of prophets, are not inherited from; whatever we leave behind is charity."

Mujahid said concerning His saying, {who will inherit from me and inherit from the House of Ya'qub}: his inheritance was knowledge, and Zakariyya was among the descendants of Ya'qub.

Hushaym said: Isma'il ibn Abi Khalid informed us, from Abu Salih, concerning His saying, {who will inherit from me and inherit from the House of Ya'qub}, he said: he might be a prophet, just as his forefathers were prophets.

Abd al-Razzaq said, from Ma'mar, from Qatadah, from al-Hasan: he inherits his prophethood and his knowledge.

Al-Suddi said: he inherits my prophethood and the prophethood of the House of Ya'qub.

From Malik, from Zayd ibn Aslam: {and inherit from the House of Ya'qub}, he said: their prophethood.

Jabir ibn Nuh and Yazid ibn Harun both said, from Isma'il ibn Abi Khalid, from Abu Salih, concerning His saying, {who will inherit from me and inherit from the House of Ya'qub}, he said: he inherits my wealth, and he inherits prophethood from the House of Ya'qub.

This is the position chosen by Ibn Jarir in his tafsir.

Abd al-Razzaq said: Ma'mar informed us, from Qatadah, that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: "May Allah have mercy on Zakariyya, he had no worry over any heirs; and may Allah have mercy on Lut, he used to take refuge in a strong support."

Ibn Jarir said: [chain] Abu Kurayb told us, Jabir ibn Nuh told us, from Mubarak, that is, ibn Fadalah, from al-Hasan, who said: the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: "May Allah have mercy on my brother Zakariyya, he had no concern over the inheritance of his wealth, when he said: {So grant me from Yourself an heir, who will inherit from me and inherit from the House of Ya'qub}." These are mursal (broken-chain) reports and do not contradict the authentic ones. And Allah knows best.

His saying, {and make him, my Lord, pleasing}, means: pleasing to You and to Your creation, whom You love and cause to be loved by Your creation, in his religion and his character.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

تَفْسِيرُ سُورَةِ مَرْيَمَ [عَلَيْهَا السَّلَامُ] 

وَهِيَ مَكِّيَّةٌ.

وَقَدْ رَوَى مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ فِي السِّيرَةِ مِنْ حَدِيثِ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ، وَأَحْمَدَ بْنِ حَنْبَلٍ عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ فِي قِصَّةِ الْهِجْرَةِ إِلَى أَرْضِ الْحَبَشَةِ مِنْ مَكَّةَ: أَنَّ جَعْفَرَ بْنَ أَبِي طَالِبٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَرَأَ صَدْرَ هَذِهِ السُّورَةِ عَلَى النَّجَاشِيِّ وَأَصْحَابِهِ .

بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ

* *

أَمَّا الْكَلَامُ عَلَى الْحُرُوفِ الْمُقَطَّعَةِ فَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ فِي أَوَّلِ سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿ذِكْرُ رَحْمَةِ رَبِّكَ﴾ أَيْ: هَذَا ذِكْرُ رَحْمَةِ اللَّهِ بِعَبْدِهِ زَكَرِيَّا.

وَقَرَأَ يَحْيَى بْنُ يَعْمَرَ "ذَكَّرَ رَحْمَةَ رَبِّكَ عَبْدَهُ زَكَريَّا".

[وَ] ﴿زَكَرِيَّا﴾ : يُمَدُّ وَيُقْصَرُ قِرَاءَتَانِ مَشْهُورَتَانِ. وَكَانَ نَبِيًّا عَظِيمًا مِنْ أَنْبِيَاءِ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ. وَفِي صَحِيحِ الْبُخَارِيِّ: أَنَّهُ كَانَ نَجَّارًا، أَيْ: كَانَ يَأْكُلُ مِنْ عَمَلِ يَدَيْهِ فِي النِّجَارَةِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿إِذْ نَادَى رَبَّهُ نِدَاءً خَفِيًّا﴾ : قَالَ بَعْضُ الْمُفَسِّرِينَ: إِنَّمَا أَخْفَى دُعَاءَهُ، لِئَلَّا يُنْسَبَ فِي طَلَبِ الْوَلَدِ إِلَى الرُّعُونَةِ لِكِبَرِهِ. حَكَاهُ المَاوَرْدِيُّ.

وَقَالَ آخَرُونَ: إِنَّمَا أَخْفَاهُ لِأَنَّهُ أَحَبُّ إِلَى اللَّهِ. كَمَا قَالَ قَتَادَةُ فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ ﴿إِذْ نَادَى رَبَّهُ نِدَاءً خَفِيًّا﴾ : إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَعْلَمُ الْقَلْبَ التَّقِيَّ ، وَيَسْمَعُ الصَّوْتَ الْخَفِيَّ.

وَقَالَ بَعْضُ السَّلَفِ: قَامَ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، وَقَدْ نَامَ أَصْحَابُهُ، فَجَعَلَ يَهْتِفُ بِرَبِّهِ يَقُولُ خُفْيَةً: يَا رَبِّ، يَا رَبِّ، يَا رَبِّ فَقَالَ اللَّهُ: لَبَّيْكَ، لَبَّيْكَ، لَبَّيْكَ.

﴿قَالَ رَبِّ إِنِّي وَهَنَ الْعَظْمُ مِنِّي﴾ أَيْ: ضَعُفَتْ وَخَارَتِ الْقُوَى، ﴿وَاشْتَعَلَ الرَّأْسُ شَيْبًا﴾ أَيِ اضْطَرَمَ الْمَشِيبُ فِي السَّوَادِ، كَمَا قَالَ ابْنُ دُرَيد فِي مَقْصُورَتِهِ :

إمَّا تَرَى رأسِي حَاكى لونُهُ ... طُرَّةَ صُْبحٍ تَحتَ أذْيَال الدُّجى ...

واشْتَعَل المُبْيَض فِي مُسْوَدّه ... مِثْلَ اشتِعَال النَّارِ في جَمْرِ الغَضَا ...

وَالْمُرَادُ مِنْ هَذَا: الْإِخْبَارُ عَنِ الضَّعْفِ وَالْكِبَرِ، وَدَلَائِلِهِ الظَّاهِرَةِ وَالْبَاطِنَةِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَلَمْ أَكُنْ بِدُعَائِكَ رَبِّ شَقِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: وَلَمْ أَعْهَدْ مِنْكَ إِلَّا الْإِجَابَةَ فِي الدُّعَاءِ، وَلَمْ تَرُدَّنِي قَطُّ فِيمَا سَأَلْتُكَ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَإِنِّي خِفْتُ الْمَوَالِيَ مِنْ وَرَائِي﴾ : قَرَأَ الْأَكْثَرُونَ بِنَصْبِ "الْيَاءِ" مِنَ ﴿الْمَوَالِيَ﴾ عَلَى أَنَّهُ مَفْعُولٌ، وَعَنِ الْكِسَائِيِّ أَنَّهُ سَكَّنَ الْيَاءَ، كَمَا قَالَ الشَّاعِرُ:

كَأنَّ أيْديهنّ في القَاع الفَرقْ ... أَيْدِي جَوَارٍ يَتَعَاطَينَ الوَرقْ 

وَقَالَ الْآخَرُ:

فَتَى لو يُبَاري الشَّمسَ ألْقَتْ قِنَاعَها ... أَوِ القَمَرَ السَّاري لألْقَى المقَالدَا ...

وَمِنْهُ قَوْلُ أَبِي تَمَّامٍ حَبِيبِ بْنِ أَوْسٍ الطَّائِيِّ:

تَغَاير الشَّعرُ فِيهِ إِذْ سَهرت لَهُ ... حَتَّى ظَنَنْتُ قَوَافِيهِ ستَقتتلُ 

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ، وقَتَادَةُ، وَالسُّدِّيُّ: أَرَادَ بِالْمَوَالِي الْعَصَبَةَ. وَقَالَ أَبُو صَالِحٍ: الْكَلَالَةَ.

وَرُوِيَ عَنْ أَمِيرِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَفَّانَ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَقْرَؤُهَا: "وَإِنِّي خَفَّت الْمَوَالِي مِنْ وَرَائِي" بِتَشْدِيدِ الْفَاءِ بِمَعْنَى: قَلَّتْ عَصَبَاتِي مِنْ بَعْدِي.

وَعَلَى الْقِرَاءَةِ الْأُولَى، وَجْهُ خَوْفِهِ أَنَّهُ خَشِيَ أَنْ يَتَصَرَّفُوا [مِنْ] بَعْدِهِ فِي النَّاسِ تَصَرُّفًا سَيِّئًا، فَسَأَلَ اللَّهَ وَلَدَا، يَكُونُ نَبِيًّا مِنْ بَعْدِهِ، لِيَسُوسَهُمْ بِنُبُوَّتِهِ وَمَا يُوحَى إِلَيْهِ. فَأُجِيبَ فِي ذَلِكَ، لَا أَنَّهُ خَشِيَ مِنْ وِرَاثَتِهِمْ لَهُ مَالَهُ، فَإِنَّ النَّبِيَّ أَعْظَمُ مَنْزِلَةً وَأَجَلُّ قَدْرًا مِنْ أَنْ يُشْفِقَ عَلَى مَالِهِ إِلَى مَا هَذَا حَدُّهُ أَنْ يَأْنَفَ مِنْ وِرَاثَةِ عَصَبَاتِهِ لَهُ، وَيَسْأَلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ، فَيَحُوزَ مِيرَاثَهُ دُونَهُ دُونَهُمْ. هَذَا وَجْهٌ.

الثَّانِي: أَنَّهُ لَمْ يُذْكَرْ أَنَّهُ كَانَ ذَا مَالٍ، بَلْ كَانَ نَجَّارًا يَأْكُلُ مِنْ كَسْبِ يَدَيْهِ، وَمِثْلُ هَذَا لَا يَجْمَعُ مَالًا وَلَا سِيَّمَا الْأَنْبِيَاءُ، عَلَيْهِمُ السَّلَامُ، فَإِنَّهُمْ كَانُوا أَزْهَدَ شَيْءٍ فِي الدُّنْيَا.

الثَّالِثُ: أَنَّهُ قَدْ ثَبَتَ فِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ وَجْهٍ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: "لَا نُورَث، مَا تَرَكْنَا فَهُوَ صَدَقَةٌ" وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ عِنْدَ التِّرْمِذِيِّ بِإِسْنَادٍ صَحِيحٍ: "نَحْنُ مَعْشَرَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ لَا نُورَثُ" وَعَلَى هَذَا فَتَعَيَّنَ حَمْلُ قَوْلِهِ: ﴿فَهَبْ لِي مِنْ لَدُنْكَ وَلِيًّا * يَرِثُنِي﴾ عَلَى مِيرَاثِ النُّبُوَّةِ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿وَيَرِثُ مِنْ آلِ يَعْقُوبَ﴾ ، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَوَرِثَ سُلَيْمَانُ دَاوُدَ﴾ [النَّمْلِ: ١٦] أَيْ: فِي النُّبُوَّةِ؛ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَ فِي الْمَالِ لَمَا خَصَّهُ مِنْ بَيْنِ إِخْوَتِهِ بِذَلِكَ، وَلَمَا كَانَ فِي الْإِخْبَارِ بِذَلِكَ كَبِيرُ فَائِدَةٍ، إِذْ مِنَ الْمَعْلُومِ الْمُسْتَقِرِّ فِي جَمِيعِ الشَّرَائِعِ وَالْمِلَلِ أَنَّ الْوَلَدَ يَرِثُ أَبَاهُ، فَلَوْلَا أَنَّهَا وِرَاثَةٌ خَاصَّةٌ لَمَا أَخْبَرَ بِهَا، وَكُلُّ هَذَا يُقَرِّرُهُ وَيُثْبِتُهُ مَا صَحَّ فِي الْحَدِيثِ: "نَحْنُ مُعَاشِرَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ لَا نُورَثُ، مَا تَرَكَنَا فَهُوَ صَدَقَةٌ".

قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿يَرِثُنِي وَيَرِثُ مِنْ آلِ يَعْقُوبَ﴾ [قَالَ] : كَانَ وِرَاثَتُهُ عِلْمًا وَكَانَ زَكَرِيَّا مِنْ ذُرِّيَّةِ يَعْقُوبَ.

وَقَالَ هُشَيْمٌ: أَخْبَرَنَا إِسْمَاعِيلَ بْنِ أَبِي خَالِدٍ، عَنْ أَبِي صَالِحٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿يَرِثُنِي وَيَرِثُ مِنْ آلِ يَعْقُوبَ﴾ قَالَ: [قَدْ] يَكُونُ نَبِيًّا كَمَا كَانَتْ آبَاؤُهُ أَنْبِيَاءَ.

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، عَنْ مَعْمَرٍ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ، عَنِ الْحَسَنِ: يَرِثُ نُبُوَّتَهُ وَعِلْمَهُ.

وَقَالَ السُّدِّي: يَرِثُ نُبُوَّتِي وَنُبُوَّةَ آلِ يَعْقُوبَ.

وَعَنْ مَالِكٍ، عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: ﴿وَيَرِثُ مِنْ آلِ يَعْقُوبَ﴾ قَالَ: نُبُوَّتَهُمْ.

وَقَالَ جَابِرُ بْنُ نُوحٍ وَيَزِيدُ بْنُ هَارُونَ، كِلَاهُمَا عَنْ إِسْمَاعِيلَ بْنِ أَبِي خَالِدٍ، عَنْ أَبِي صالح في قَوْلِهِ: ﴿يَرِثُنِي وَيَرِثُ مِنْ آلِ يَعْقُوبَ﴾ قَالَ: يَرِثُ مَالِي، وَيَرِثُ مِنْ آلِ يَعْقُوبَ النُّبُوَّةَ.

وَهَذَا اخْتِيَارُ ابْنِ جَرِيرٍ فِي تَفْسِيرِهِ.

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ: أَخْبَرَنَا مَعْمَرٌ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وسلم قال: "يَرْحَمُ اللَّهُ زَكَرِيَّا، وَمَا كَانَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ وَرَثَةٍ، وَيَرْحَمُ اللَّهُ لُوطًا، إِنْ كَانَ لَيَأْوِي إِلَى رُكْنٍ شَدِيدٍ" 

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو كُرَيْب، حَدَّثَنَا جَابِرُ بْنُ نُوحٍ، عَنْ مُبَارَكٍ -هُوَ ابْنُ فَضَالَةَ -عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وسلم: "رَحِمَ اللَّهُ أَخِي زَكَرِيَّا، مَا كَانَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ وَرَثَةِ مَالِهِ حِينَ يَقُولُ: ﴿فَهَبْ لِي مِنْ لَدُنْكَ وَلِيًّا * يَرِثُنِي وَيَرِثُ مِنْ آلِ يَعْقُوبَ﴾ وَهَذِهِ مُرْسَلَاتٌ لَا تُعَارِضُ الصِّحَاحَ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَاجْعَلْهُ رَبِّ رَضِيًّا﴾ أَيْ مَرْضِيًّا عِنْدَكَ وَعِنْدَ خَلْقِكِ، تُحِبُّهُ وَتُحَبِّبُهُ إِلَى خَلْقِكَ فِي دِينِهِ وَخُلُقِهِ.

---

## 19:7 — verse 7

### Translation

This statement contains an ellipsis, namely that he was answered in what he had asked for in his supplication, and it was said [to him]: {O Zakariyya, indeed We give you glad tidings of a boy whose name is Yahya}, just as the Almighty said: {There Zakariyya called upon his Lord, saying: My Lord, grant me from Yourself pure offspring, indeed You are the Hearer of supplication. Then the angels called out to him while he stood praying in the sanctuary: Allah gives you glad tidings of Yahya, confirming a word from Allah, a master, one who abstains, and a prophet from among the righteous} [Al Imran: 38, 39].

Regarding His saying: {We have not made for him before any namesake}, Qatadah, Ibn Jurayj, and Ibn Zayd said: meaning, no one before him had been named with this name. Ibn Jarir, may Allah have mercy on him, chose this view.

Mujahid said: {We have not made for him before any namesake} means: a likeness.

He derived this from the meaning of His saying: {So worship Him and be patient in worshipping Him. Do you know of any likeness to Him?} [Maryam: 65], meaning: a similitude.

Ali ibn Abi Talhah reported from Ibn Abbas: meaning, no barren women before him had given birth to one like him.

This is evidence that Zakariyya (peace be upon him) was one to whom no child was born, and likewise his wife had been barren from the beginning of her life, unlike Ibrahim and Sarah (peace be upon them), for the two of them only marveled at the glad tidings of Ishaq because of their old age, not because of barrenness. This is why he said: {Do you give me glad tidings though old age has touched me? Then of what do you give me glad tidings?} [Al-Hijr: 54], despite the fact that Ismail had already been born to him thirteen years before that. And his wife said: {Woe to me! Shall I bear a child while I am an old woman and this, my husband, is an old man? Indeed this is a strange thing. They said: Do you marvel at the decree of Allah? The mercy of Allah and His blessings be upon you, O people of the house. Indeed He is Praiseworthy, Glorious} [Hud: 72, 73].

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

هَذَا الْكَلَامُ يَتَضَمَّنُ مَحْذُوفًا، وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ أُجِيبَ إِلَى مَا سَأَلَ فِي دُعَائِهِ فَقِيلَ [لَهُ] : ﴿يَا زَكَرِيَّا إِنَّا نُبَشِّرُكَ بِغُلامٍ اسْمُهُ يَحْيَى﴾ ، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿هُنَالِكَ دَعَا زَكَرِيَّا رَبَّهُ قَالَ رَبِّ هَبْ لِي مِنْ لَدُنْكَ ذُرِّيَّةً طَيِّبَةً إِنَّكَ سَمِيعُ الدُّعَاءِ فَنَادَتْهُ الْمَلائِكَةُ وَهُوَ قَائِمٌ يُصَلِّي فِي الْمِحْرَابِ أَنَّ اللَّهَ يُبَشِّرُكَ بِيَحْيَى مُصَدِّقًا بِكَلِمَةٍ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَسَيِّدًا وَحَصُورًا وَنَبِيًّا مِنَ الصَّالِحِينَ﴾ [آلِ عِمْرَانَ: ٣٨، ٣٩]

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿لَمْ نَجْعَلْ لَهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ سَمِيًّا﴾ قَالَ قَتَادَةُ، وَابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ، وَابْنُ زَيْدٍ: أَيْ لَمْ يُسَمَّ أَحَدٌ قَبْلَهُ بِهَذَا الِاسْمِ، وَاخْتَارَهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ، رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ.

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: ﴿لَمْ نَجْعَلْ لَهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ سَمِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: شَبِيهًا.

أَخَذَهُ مِنْ مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ: ﴿فَاعْبُدْهُ وَاصْطَبِرْ لِعِبَادَتِهِ هَلْ تَعْلَمُ لَهُ سَمِيًّا﴾ [مَرْيَمَ: ٦٥] أَيْ: شَبِيهًا.

وَقَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: أَيْ لَمْ تَلِدِ الْعَوَاقِرُ قَبْلَهُ مِثْلَهُ.

وَهَذَا دَلِيلٌ عَلَى أَنَّ زَكَرِيَّا عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، كَانَ لَا يُوْلَدُ لَهُ، وَكَذَلِكَ امْرَأَتُهُ كَانَتْ عَاقِرًا مِنْ أَوَّلِ عُمْرِهَا، بِخِلَافِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَسَارَةَ، عَلَيْهِمَا السَّلَامُ، فَإِنَّهُمَا إِنَّمَا تَعَجَّبَا مِنَ الْبِشَارَةِ بِإِسْحَاقَ عَلَى كِبَرِهِمَا لَا لِعُقْرِهِمَا ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿أَبَشَّرْتُمُونِي عَلَى أَنْ مَسَّنِيَ الْكِبَرُ فَبِمَ تُبَشِّرُونِ﴾ [الْحِجْرِ: ٥٤] مَعَ أَنَّهُ كَانَ قَدْ وُلِدَ لَهُ قَبْلَهُ إسماعيل بثلاث عشرة سنة. وقالت امرأته: ﴿يَا وَيْلَتَى أَأَلِدُ وَأَنَا عَجُوزٌ وَهَذَا بَعْلِي شَيْخًا إِنَّ هَذَا لَشَيْءٌ عَجِيبٌ * قَالُوا أَتَعْجَبِينَ مِنْ أَمْرِ اللَّهِ رَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ عَلَيْكُمْ أَهْلَ الْبَيْتِ إِنَّهُ حَمِيدٌ مَجِيدٌ﴾ [هُودٍ: ٧٢، ٧٣] .

---

## 19:8-9 — verses 8-9 (shared commentary)

### Translation

This is an expression of astonishment from Zakariyya (peace be upon him), when he was granted what he had asked for and given the good news of a child, so he rejoiced greatly, and asked about the manner in which the child would be born to him, and the way through which the child would come to him, given that his wife was barren and had not given birth from the beginning of her life despite her advanced age, and given that he himself had grown old and reached *`utiyya*, meaning his bones had become hard and brittle, and there remained in him neither the capacity to impregnate nor to have relations.

The Arabs say of a piece of wood when it dries out: "*`ata ya`tu `utiyyan wa `utuwwan*, and *`asa ya`su `usuwwan wa `isiyya*."

Mujahid said: {`itiyya} means the brittleness of the bone.

Ibn Abbas and others said: {`itiyya} means old age.

The apparent meaning is that it is more specific than mere old age.

Ibn Jarir said: [chain] Yaqub told us, Hushaym told us, Husayn informed us, from Ikrimah, from Ibn Abbas, who said: I have known the entire Sunnah, except that I do not know whether the Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to recite aloud in the Zuhr and Asr prayers or not, and I do not know how he used to recite this word: {and I have reached from old age `itiyya} or "`isiyya."

Imam Ahmad related it from Surayj ibn al-Nu'man, and Abu Dawud from Ziyad ibn Ayyub, both of them from Hushaym, with this wording.

{He said}, meaning the angel, answering Zakariyya regarding what he found astonishing: {Thus said your Lord: it is easy for Me}, meaning: bringing a child into being from you and from this wife of yours, not from another, {is easy}, meaning: it is simple and effortless for Allah.

Then He mentioned to him something even more astonishing than what he had asked about, saying: {And I created you before, when you were nothing}, just as He, exalted is He, said: {Has there not come upon man a period of time when he was not a thing remembered?} [al-Insan: 1]

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

هَذَا تَعَجُّبٌ مِنْ زَكَرِيَّا، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، حِينَ أُجِيبَ إِلَى مَا سَأَلَ، وبُشِّر بِالْوَلَدِ، فَفَرِحَ فَرَحًا شَدِيدًا، وَسَأَلَ عَنْ كَيْفِيَّةِ مَا يُولَدُ لَهُ، وَالْوَجْهُ الَّذِي يَأْتِيهِ مِنْهُ الْوَلَدُ، مَعَ أَنَّ امْرَأَتَهُ [كَانَتْ] عَاقِرًا لَمْ تَلِدْ مِنْ أَوَّلِ عُمْرِهَا مَعَ كِبَرِهَا، وَمَعَ أَنَّهُ قَدْ كَبُرَ وَعَتَا، أَيْ عَسَا عَظْمُهُ وَنَحُلَ وَلَمْ يَبْقَ فِيهِ لِقَاحٌ وَلَا جِمَاعٌ.

تَقُولُ الْعَرَبُ لِلْعُودِ إِذَا يَبِسَ: "عَتا يَعْتو عِتيا وعُتُوا، وعَسا يَعْسو عُسوا وعِسيا".

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: ﴿عِتِيًّا﴾ بِمَعْنَى: نُحُولِ الْعَظْمِ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ وَغَيْرُهُ: ﴿عِتِيًّا﴾ يَعْنِي: الْكِبَرَ.

وَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ أَخَصُّ مِنَ الْكِبَرِ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا يَعْقُوبُ، حَدَّثَنَا هُشَيْم، أَخْبَرَنَا حُصَيْن، عَنْ عِكْرمة، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: لَقَدْ عَلِمْتُ السُّنَّةَ كُلَّهَا، غَيْرَ أَنِّي لَا أَدْرِي أَكَانَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقْرَأُ فِي الظُّهْرِ وَالْعَصْرِ أَمْ لَا؟ وَلَا أَدْرِي كَيْفَ كَانَ يَقْرَأُ هَذَا الْحَرْفَ: ﴿وَقَدْ بَلَغْتُ مِنَ الْكِبَرِ عِتِيًّا﴾ أَوْ "عِسِيًّا".

وَرَوَاهُ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ عَنْ سُرَيْج بْنِ النُّعْمَانِ، وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ، عَنْ زِيَادِ بْنِ أَيُّوبَ، كِلَاهُمَا عَنْ هُشَيْمٍ، بِهِ.

﴿قَالَ﴾ أَيِ الْمَلَكُ مُجِيبًا لِزَكَرِيَّا عَمَّا اسْتَعْجَبَ مِنْهُ: ﴿كَذَلِكَ قَالَ رَبُّكَ هُوَ عَلَيَّ هَيِّنٌ﴾ أَيْ: إِيجَادُ الْوَلَدِ مِنْكَ وَمَنْ زَوْجَتِكَ هَذِهِ لَا مِنْ غَيْرِهَا ﴿هَيِّنٌ﴾ أَيْ: يَسِيرٌ سَهْلٌ عَلَى اللَّهِ.

ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ لَهُ مَا هُوَ أَعْجَبُ مِمَّا سَأَلَ عَنْهُ، فَقَالَ: ﴿وَقَدْ خَلَقْتُكَ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَلَمْ تَكُ شَيْئًا﴾ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿هَلْ أَتَى عَلَى الإنْسَانِ حِينٌ مِنَ الدَّهْرِ لَمْ يَكُنْ شَيْئًا مَذْكُورًا﴾ [الْإِنْسَانُ: ١]

---

## 19:10-11 — verses 10-11 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Exalted says, informing about Zakariyya, peace be upon him, that he {said, "My Lord, appoint for me a sign,"} meaning a mark and an indication of the occurrence of what You promised me, so that my soul may settle and my heart find rest through what You promised me, just as Ibrahim, peace be upon him, said: {"My Lord, show me how You give life to the dead." He said, "Have you not believed?" He said, "Yes, but that my heart may be at rest,"} the verse [al-Baqarah: 260]. {He said, "Your sign} meaning your mark {is that you shall not speak to the people for three nights while being sound,"} meaning that you shall restrain your tongue from speech for three nights while you are healthy and sound, without any sickness or ailment.

Ibn Abbas, Mujahid, Ikrimah, Wahb [ibn Munabbih], al-Suddi, Qatadah, and more than one other said: his tongue was seized without any sickness.

Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: he would recite and glorify God but could not speak to his people except by gesture.

Al-Awfi reported from Ibn Abbas: {"three nights while being sound"} meaning consecutive.

The first opinion, from him and from the majority, is more correct, as the Exalted said at [the beginning of] Al Imran: {He said, "My Lord, appoint for me a sign." He said, "Your sign is that you shall not speak to the people for three days except by gesture. And remember your Lord much and glorify Him in the evening and the morning"} [Al Imran: 41]. Malik reported from Zayd ibn Aslam: {"three nights while being sound"} meaning without muteness.

This is evidence that he was not able to speak to the people during these three nights and their days {except by gesture}, meaning by signaling. Therefore He says in this noble verse: {So he came out to his people from the sanctuary,} meaning the one in which he had been given the glad tidings of the child, {and he signaled to them,} meaning he made a hidden, rapid gesture, {that you should glorify morning and evening,} meaning in agreement with what he himself had been commanded to do during these three days, in addition to his own acts, and as thanks to God for what He had bestowed upon him.

Mujahid said: {"and he signaled to them"} meaning he gestured. Wahb and Qatadah said the same.

Mujahid said in another report from him: {"and he signaled to them"} meaning he wrote for them on the ground. Al-Suddi said likewise.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى مُخْبِرًا عَنْ زَكَرِيَّا، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، أَنَّهُ ﴿قَالَ رَبِّ اجْعَلْ لِي آيَةً﴾ أَيْ: عَلَامَةً وَدَلِيلًا عَلَى وُجُودِ مَا وَعَدْتَنِي، لِتَسْتَقِرَّ نَفْسِي وَيَطْمَئِنَّ قَلْبِي بِمَا وَعَدْتَنِي كَمَا قَالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: ﴿رَبِّ أَرِنِي كَيْفَ تُحْيِ الْمَوْتَى قَالَ أَوَلَمْ تُؤْمِنْ قَالَ بَلَى وَلَكِنْ لِيَطْمَئِنَّ قَلْبِي﴾ الْآيَةَ [الْبَقَرَةِ: ٢٦٠] . ﴿قَالَ آيَتُكَ﴾ أَيْ: عَلَامَتُكَ ﴿أَلا تُكَلِّمَ النَّاسَ ثَلاثَ لَيَالٍ سَوِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: أَنْ تَحْبِسَ لِسَانَكَ عَنِ الْكَلَامِ ثَلَاثَ لَيَالٍ وَأَنْتَ صَحِيحٌ سَوِيٌّ مِنْ غَيْرِ مَرَضٍ وَلَا عِلَّةٍ 

قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ، وَمُجَاهِدٌ، وَعِكْرِمَةُ، وَوَهْبُ [بْنُ مُنَبِّهٍ] ، وَالسُّدِّيُّ وقَتَادَةُ وَغَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ: اعْتُقِلَ لِسَانُهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ مَرَضٍ.

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: كَانَ يَقْرَأُ وَيُسَبِّحُ وَلَا يَسْتَطِيعُ أَنْ يُكَلِّمَ قَوْمَهُ إِلَّا إِشَارَةً.

وَقَالَ الْعَوْفِيُّ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿ثَلاثَ لَيَالٍ سَوِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: مُتَتَابِعَاتٍ.

وَالْقَوْلُ الْأَوَّلُ عَنْهُ وَعَنِ الْجُمْهُورِ أَصَحُّ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي [أَوَّلِ] آلِ عِمْرَانَ: ﴿قَالَ رَبِّ اجْعَلْ لِي آيَةً قَالَ آيَتُكَ أَلا تُكَلِّمَ النَّاسَ ثَلاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ إِلا رَمْزًا وَاذْكُرْ رَبَّكَ كَثِيرًا وَسَبِّحْ بِالْعَشِيِّ وَالإبْكَارِ﴾ [آلِ عِمْرَانَ: ٤١] وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ، عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: ﴿ثَلاثَ لَيَالٍ سَوِيًّا﴾ مِنْ غَيْرِ خَرَسٍ.

وَهَذَا دَلِيلٌ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ يُكَلِّمُ النَّاسَ فِي هَذِهِ اللَّيَالِي الثَّلَاثِ وَأَيَّامِهَا ﴿إِلا رَمْزًا﴾ أَيْ: إِشَارَةً؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ الْكَرِيمَةِ: ﴿فَخَرَجَ عَلَى قَوْمِهِ مِنَ الْمِحْرَابِ﴾ أَيِ: الَّذِي بُشِّرَ فِيهِ بِالْوَلَدِ، ﴿فَأَوْحَى إِلَيْهِمْ﴾ أَيْ: أَشَارَ إِشَارَةً خَفِيَّةً سَرِيعَةً: ﴿أَنْ سَبِّحُوا بُكْرَةً وَعَشِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: مُوَافَقَةً لَهُ فِيمَا أُمِرَ بِهِ فِي هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ الثَّلَاثَةِ زِيَادَةً عَلَى أَعْمَالِهِ، وَشُكْرًا لِلَّهِ عَلَى مَا أَوْلَاهُ.

قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: ﴿فَأَوْحَى إِلَيْهِمْ﴾ أَيْ: أَشَارَ. وَبِهِ قَالَ وَهْبٌ، وقَتَادَةُ.

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ فِي رِوَايَةٍ عَنْهُ: ﴿فَأَوْحَى إِلَيْهِمْ﴾ أَيْ: كَتَبَ لَهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ، كَذَا قَالَ السدي.

---

## 19:12-15 — verses 12-15 (shared commentary)

### Translation

This too contains an ellipsis, whose implied meaning is: that he found this boy who had been announced, namely Yahya (peace be upon him), and that God taught him the Book, which is the Torah that they used to study among themselves, and by which the prophets who submitted judged for those who were Jews, along with the rabbis and the scholars. His age at that time was young, and for this reason his mention was highlighted, along with what God bestowed upon him and upon his parents, so He said: {O Yahya, take the Book with strength}, meaning: learn the Book {with strength}, meaning: with earnestness, eagerness, and diligence. {And We gave him judgment while he was a boy}, meaning: understanding, knowledge, earnestness, resolve, devotion to good, dedication to it, and striving in it, while he was young, of tender age.

Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: Ma'mar said: The boys said to Yahya ibn Zakariyya, "Come, let us play." He said, "I was not created for play." He said: it was for this reason that God revealed: {And We gave him judgment while he was a boy}.

Regarding His saying, {and tenderness from Us}: Ali ibn Abi Talha reported from Ibn Abbas concerning {and tenderness from Us} that he said: and mercy from Us. Ikrimah, Qatadah, and al-Dahhak said likewise, and added: which no one but Us has power over. Qatadah added: Zakariyya was shown mercy through it.

Mujahid said: {and tenderness from Us} means: and compassion from his Lord toward him.

Ikrimah said regarding {and tenderness from Us}: he said, love for him. Ibn Zayd said: as for hanan, it is love. Ata ibn Abi Rabah said regarding {and tenderness from Us}: he said, exaltation from Us.

Ibn Jurayj said: Amr ibn Dinar informed me that he heard Ikrimah report from Ibn Abbas who said: No, by God, I do not know what hanan means.

Ibn Jarir said: [chain] Mansur said: I asked Sa'id ibn Jubayr about His saying, {and tenderness from Us}, and he said: I asked Ibn Abbas about it, and he could give no answer regarding it.

What is apparent from this context is that {and tenderness from Us} is connected to His saying {And We gave him judgment while he was a boy}, meaning: We gave him judgment and tenderness, {and purity}, meaning: and We made him possessed of tenderness and purity. So hanan is love accompanied by compassion and inclination, as the Arabs say: the she-camel yearned (hannat) toward her young, and the woman yearned toward her husband. From this a woman is named "Hannah," from al-hannah. And a man yearns (hanna) toward his homeland. From this also come compassion and mercy, as the poet said:

Show tenderness toward me, may the Sovereign guide you, for every situation has its proper speech.

In the Musnad of Imam Ahmad, from Anas, may God be pleased with him, the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "A man will remain in the Fire calling out for a thousand years: O Hannan, O Mannan."

This may be doubled in form, and some consider what has come of it to be a distinct linguistic usage on its own, as Tarafah said:

I am Mundhir, you have destroyed, so spare some of us. Hananayka (have mercy twice over), for some harm is lighter than other harm.

Regarding His saying, {and purity}: it is connected to {and tenderness}. So zakah (purity) is cleanliness from defilement, sins, and transgressions.

Qatadah said: zakah is righteous action.

Al-Dahhak and Ibn Jurayj said: righteous, pure action.

Al-Awfi reported from Ibn Abbas: {and purity} he said: blessing. {And he was pious}: he was pure, and he never committed a sin.

Regarding His saying, {and dutiful to his parents, and he was not a tyrant, disobedient}: After the Exalted mentioned his obedience to his Lord, and that He created him possessed of mercy, purity, and piety, He followed with mention of his obedience to his parents and his dutifulness toward them, and his avoidance of disobedience to them, in word, deed, command, and prohibition. For this reason He said: {and he was not a tyrant, disobedient}. Then, after these beautiful qualities, as a reward for that, He said: {And peace be upon him the day he was born, and the day he dies, and the day he is raised alive}, meaning: he has security in these three states.

Sufyan ibn Uyaynah said: The most terrifying moments for a created being are three: the day he is born, when he sees himself emerging from what he was in; the day he dies, when he sees a people he had not previously beheld; and the day he is raised, when he sees himself in a mighty gathering. He said: So God honored Yahya ibn Zakariyya in these, singling him out with peace upon him: {And peace be upon him the day he was born, and the day he dies, and the day he is raised alive}.

Ibn Jarir related this from Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Marwazi, from Sadaqah ibn al-Fadl, from him.

Abd al-Razzaq said: Ma'mar informed us, from Qatadah, regarding His saying {a tyrant, disobedient}, he said: Ibn al-Musayyib used to mention, he said: The Prophet ﷺ said: "There is no one who will meet God on the Day of Resurrection except one who has a sin, except Yahya ibn Zakariyya." Qatadah said: He never sinned nor even inclined toward a woman. [This is] mursal (a report missing its final link to the Companion).

Muhammad ibn Ishaq said, from Yahya ibn Sa'id, from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib: Ibn al-'As related to me that he heard the Messenger of God ﷺ say: "Every son of Adam comes on the Day of Resurrection having a sin, except for what was the case with Yahya ibn Zakariyya." This Ibn Ishaq is a mudallis (one who conceals defects in transmission), and he related this hadith with an ambiguous form of attribution ("an"), so God knows best.

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Ali ibn Zayd, from Yusuf ibn Mihran, from Ibn Abbas, that the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "There is no one among the children of Adam except that he has erred or inclined toward an error, except Yahya ibn Zakariyya. And it is not fitting for anyone to say: I am better than Yunus ibn Matta."

This too is weak, because Ali ibn Zayd ibn Jud'an has many objectionable reports, and God knows best.

Sa'id ibn Abi Arubah said, from Qatadah: that al-Hasan said: Yahya and Isa (peace be upon them both) met, and Isa said to him: "Ask forgiveness for me, you are better than I am." The other said to him: "Ask forgiveness for me, for you are better than I am." Then Isa said to him: "You are better than I am. I greeted myself with peace, while God greeted you with peace." And by God, their merit became known.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

وَهَذَا أَيْضًا تَضَمَّنَ مَحْذُوفًا، تَقْدِيرُهُ: أَنَّهُ وَجَدَ هَذَا الْغُلَامَ الْمُبَشَّرَ بِهِ، وَهُوَ يَحْيَى، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ عَلَّمَهُ الْكِتَابَ، وَهُوَ التَّوْرَاةُ الَّتِي كَانُوا يَتَدَارَسُونَهَا بَيْنَهُمْ، وَيَحْكُمُ بِهَا النَّبِيُّونَ الَّذِينَ أَسْلَمُوا لِلَّذِينَ هَادُوا وَالرَّبَّانِيُّونَ وَالْأَحْبَارُ. وَقَدْ كَانَ سِنُّهُ إِذْ ذَاكَ صَغِيرًا، فَلِهَذَا نَوَّهَ بِذِكْرِهِ، وَبِمَا أَنْعَمَ بِهِ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى وَالِدَيْهِ، فَقَالَ: ﴿يَا يَحْيَى خُذِ الْكِتَابَ بِقُوَّةٍ﴾ أَيْ: تَعَلَّمِ الْكِتَابَ ﴿بِقُوَّةٍ﴾ أَيْ: بِجِدٍّ وَحِرْصٍ وَاجْتِهَادٍ ﴿وَآتَيْنَاهُ الْحُكْمَ صَبِيًّا﴾ أَيِ: الْفَهْمَ وَالْعِلْمَ وَالْجِدَّ وَالْعَزْمَ، وَالْإِقْبَالَ عَلَى الْخَيْرِ، وَالْإِكْبَابَ عَلَيْهِ، وَالِاجْتِهَادَ فِيهِ وَهُوَ صَغِيرٌ حَدَثُ [السِّنِّ] .

قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ الْمُبَارَكِ: قَالَ مَعْمَرٌ: قَالَ الصِّبْيَانُ لِيَحْيَى بْنِ زَكَرِيَّا: اذْهَبْ بِنَا نَلْعَبْ. قَالَ: مَا لِلَّعِبِ خُلِقْتُ ، قَالَ: فَلِهَذَا أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ: ﴿وَآتَيْنَاهُ الْحُكْمَ صَبِيًّا﴾ .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَحَنَانًا مِنْ لَدُنَّا﴾ قَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿وَحَنَانًا مِنْ لَدُنَّا﴾ يَقُولُ: وَرَحْمَةً مِنْ عِنْدِنَا، وَكَذَا قَالَ عِكْرِمَةُ، وقَتَادَةُ، وَالضَّحَّاكُ وَزَادَ: لَا يَقْدِرُ عَلَيْهَا غَيْرُنَا. وَزَادَ قَتَادَةُ: رُحِم بِهَا زَكَرِيَّا.

وَقَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: ﴿وَحَنَانًا مِنْ لَدُنَّا﴾ وَتَعَطُّفًا مِنْ رَبِّهِ عَلَيْهِ.

وَقَالَ عِكْرِمَةُ: ﴿وَحَنَانًا مِنْ لَدُنَّا﴾ [قَالَ: مَحَبَّةً عَلَيْهِ. وَقَالَ ابْنُ زَيْدٍ: أَمَّا الْحَنَانُ فَالْمَحَبَّةُ. وَقَالَ عَطَاءُ بْنُ أَبِي رَبَاحٍ: ﴿وَحَنَانًا مِنْ لَدُنَّا﴾ ] ، قَالَ: تعظيمًا من لدنا .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ: أَخْبَرَنِي عَمْرُو بْنُ دِينَارٍ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ عِكْرِمَةَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: لَا وَاللَّهِ مَا أَدْرِي مَا حَنَانًا.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ حُمَيْدٍ، حَدَّثَنَا جَرِيرٌ، عَنْ مَنْصُورٍ: سَأَلْتُ سَعِيدَ بْنَ جُبَيْرٍ عَنْ قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَحَنَانًا مِنْ لَدُنَّا﴾ ، فَقَالَ: سَأَلْتُ عَنْهَا عباس، فَلَمْ يَحْرِ فِيهَا شَيْئًا.

وَالظَّاهِرُ مِنْ هَذَا السِّيَاقِ أَنَّ: ﴿وَحَنَانًا [مِنْ لَدُنَّا] ﴾ مَعْطُوفٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَآتَيْنَاهُ الْحُكْمَ صَبِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: وَآتَيْنَاهُ الْحُكْمَ وَحَنَانًا، ﴿وَزَكَاةً﴾ أَيْ: وَجَعَلْنَاهُ ذَا حَنَانٍ وَزَكَاةٍ، فَالْحَنَانُ هُوَ الْمَحَبَّةُ فِي شَفَقَةٍ وَمَيْلٍ كَمَا تَقُولُ الْعَرَبُ: حَنَّتِ النَّاقَةُ عَلَى وَلَدِهَا، وَحَنَّتِ الْمَرْأَةُ عَلَى زَوْجِهَا. وَمِنْهُ سُمِّيَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ "حَنَّة" مِنَ الحَنَّة، وَحَنَّ الرَّجُلُ إِلَى وَطَنِهِ، وَمِنْهُ التَّعَطُّفُ وَالرَّحْمَةُ، كَمَا قَالَ الشَّاعِرُ 

تَحنَّنْ عَلَي هَدَاكَ المليكُ ... فإنَّ لكُل مَقامٍ مَقَالا ...

وَفِي الْمُسْنَدِ لِلْإِمَامِ أَحْمَدَ، عَنْ أَنَسٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ قَالَ: "يَبْقَى رَجُلٌ فِي النَّارِ يُنَادِي أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ: يَا حَنَّانُ يَا مَنَّانُ" 

وَقَدْ يُثنَّي وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَجْعَلُ مَا وَرَدَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ لُغَةً بِذَاتِهَا، كَمَا قَالَ طُرْفَةُ:

أَنَا مُنْذر أفنيتَ فاسْتبق بَعْضَنَا ... حَنَانَيْك بَعْض الشَّر أهْونُ مِنْ بَعْض 

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَزَكَاةً﴾ مَعْطُوفٌ عَلَى ﴿وَحَنَانًا﴾ فَالزَّكَاةُ الطَّهَارَةُ مِنَ الدَّنَسِ وَالْآثَامِ وَالذُّنُوبِ.

وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ: الزَّكَاةُ الْعَمَلُ الصَّالِحُ.

وَقَالَ الضَّحَّاكُ وَابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ: الْعَمَلُ الصَّالِحُ الزَّكِيُّ.

وَقَالَ الْعَوْفِيُّ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿وَزَكَاةً﴾ [قَالَ: بَرَكَةً] ﴿وَكَانَ تَقِيًّا﴾ طَهُرَ، فَلَمْ يَعْمَلْ بِذَنْبٍ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَبَرًّا بِوَالِدَيْهِ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ جَبَّارًا عَصِيًّا﴾ لَمَّا ذَكَرَ تَعَالَى طَاعَتَهُ لِرَبِّهِ، وَأَنَّهُ خَلَقَهُ ذَا رَحْمَةٍ وَزَكَاةٍ وَتُقًى، عَطَفَ بِذِكْرِ طَاعَتِهِ لِوَالِدَيْهِ وَبِرِّهِ بِهِمَا، وَمُجَانَبَتِهِ عُقُوقَهُمَا، قَوْلًا وَفِعْلًا [وَأَمْرًا] وَنَهْيًا؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿وَلَمْ يَكُنْ جَبَّارًا عَصِيًّا﴾ ثُمَّ قَالَ بَعْدَ هَذِهِ الْأَوْصَافِ الْجَمِيلَةِ جَزَاءً لَهُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ: ﴿وَسَلامٌ عَلَيْهِ يَوْمَ وُلِدَ وَيَوْمَ يَمُوتُ وَيَوْمَ يُبْعَثُ حَيًّا﴾ أَيْ: لَهُ الْأَمَانُ فِي هَذِهِ الثَّلَاثَةِ الْأَحْوَالِ.

وَقَالَ سُفْيَانُ بْنُ عُيَيْنَةَ: أَوْحَشُ مَا يَكُونُ الْخَلْقُ فِي ثَلَاثَةِ مَوَاطِنَ: يَوْمَ يُولَدُ، فَيَرَى نَفْسَهُ خَارِجًا مِمَّا كَانَ فِيهِ، وَيَوْمَ يَمُوتُ فَيَرَى قَوْمًا لَمْ يَكُنْ عَايَنَهُمْ، وَيَوْمَ يُبْعَثُ، فَيَرَى نَفْسَهُ فِي مَحْشَرٍ عَظِيمٍ. قَالَ: فَأَكْرَمَ اللَّهُ فِيهَا يَحْيَى بْنَ زَكَرِيَّا فَخَصَّهُ بِالسَّلَامِ عَلَيْهِ، ﴿وَسَلامٌ عَلَيْهِ يَوْمَ وُلِدَ وَيَوْمَ يَمُوتُ وَيَوْمَ يُبْعَثُ حَيًّا﴾

رَوَاهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ عَنْ أَحْمَدَ بْنِ مَنْصُورٍ الْمَرْوَزِيِّ عَنْ صَدَقَةَ بْنِ الْفَضْلِ عَنْهُ.

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ: أَخْبَرَنَا مَعْمَرٌ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ، فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿جَبَّارًا عَصِيًّا﴾ ، قَالَ: كَانَ ابْنُ الْمُسَيَّبِ يَذْكُرُ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: "مَا مِنْ أَحَدٍ يَلْقَى اللَّهَ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ إِلَّا ذَا ذَنْبٍ، إِلَّا يَحْيَى بْنَ زَكَرِيَّا". قَالَ قَتَادَةُ: مَا أَذْنَبَ وَلَا هَمَّ بِامْرَأَةٍ، مُرْسَلٌ 

وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ، عَنْ يَحْيَى بْنِ سَعِيدٍ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ الْمُسَيَّبِ، حَدَّثَنِي ابْنُ الْعَاصِ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ : "كُلُّ بَنِي آدَمَ يَأْتِي يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَلَهُ ذَنْبٌ، إِلَّا مَا كَانَ مِنْ يَحْيَى بْنِ زَكَرِيَّا" ابْنُ إِسْحَاقَ هَذَا مُدَلِّسٌ، وَقَدْ عَنْعَنَ هَذَا الْحَدِيثَ، فَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا عَفَّانُ، حَدَّثَنَا حَمَّادُ، أَخْبَرَنَا عَلِيِّ بْنِ زَيْدٍ، عَنْ يُوسُفَ بْنِ مِهْران، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: "مَا مِنْ أَحَدٍ مِنْ وَلَدِ آدَمَ إِلَّا وَقَدْ أَخْطَأَ، أَوْ همَّ بِخَطِيئَةٍ، لَيْسَ يَحْيَى بْنَ زَكَرِيَّا، وَمَا يَنْبَغِي لِأَحَدٍ أَنْ يَقُولَ: أَنَا خَيْرٌ مِنْ يُونُسَ بْنِ مَتَّى" 

وَهَذَا أَيْضًا ضَعِيفٌ؛ لِأَنَّ عَلِيُّ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنُ جُدْعَانَ لَهُ مُنْكَرَاتٌ كَثِيرَةٌ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَقَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ أَبِي عَرُوبة، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ: أَنَّ حسن قَالَ: إِنَّ يَحْيَى وَعِيسَى، عَلَيْهِمَا السَّلَامُ، الْتَقَيَا، فَقَالَ لَهُ عِيسَى: اسْتَغْفِرْ لِي، أَنْتَ خَيْرٌ مِنِّي، فَقَالَ لَهُ الْآخَرُ: اسْتَغْفِرْ لِي فَأَنْتَ خَيْرٌ مِنِّي. فَقَالَ لَهُ عِيسَى: أَنْتَ خَيْرٌ مِنِّي، سَلَّمتُ عَلَى نَفْسِي، وَسَلَّمَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْكَ، فَعرُف وَاللَّهِ فَضْلُهُمَا.

---

## 19:16-21 — verses 16-21 (shared commentary)

### Translation

When the Exalted mentioned the story of Zakariyya (peace be upon him), and how He brought forth from him, in his old age and with his wife's barrenness, a pure, clean, blessed son, He followed it with the mention of the story of Maryam, in the bringing forth of her son Isa (peace be upon them both) from her without a father. For there is a correspondence and resemblance between the two stories. This is why He mentioned them together in Al Imran, here, and in Surat al-Anbiya, joining the two stories because of the closeness between them in meaning, so as to show His servants His power and the greatness of His dominion, and that He is capable of whatever He wills. So He said: {And mention in the Book, Maryam} she is Maryam the daughter of Imran, of the lineage of Dawud (peace be upon him), and she was from a pure, good household among the Children of Israel. God the Exalted mentioned the story of her mother's giving birth to her in Al Imran, and how she vowed her as one dedicated, meaning to serve the Sacred Mosque of Bayt al-Maqdis, for that was how they sought closeness to God. {So her Lord accepted her with a good acceptance and made her grow up in a good manner} [Al Imran: 37]. She grew up among the Children of Israel in a magnificent upbringing, and became one of the worshippers and ascetics renowned for immense devotion, seclusion for worship, and diligence. She was in the care of her sister's husband, and it is also said her maternal aunt's husband, Zakariyya, who was at that time the prophet of the Children of Israel and their great leader, to whom they turned in matters of their religion. Zakariyya witnessed from her astonishing wonders that amazed him: {Every time Zakariyya entered the sanctuary to visit her, he found provision with her. He said, "O Maryam, from where does this come to you?" She said, "It is from God. Indeed God provides for whom He wills without account"} [Al Imran: 37]. It is mentioned that he would find with her the fruit of winter in summer and the fruit of summer in winter, as was explained previously in Al Imran.

Then when God the Exalted willed, and His is the wisdom and the conclusive proof, to bring forth from her His servant and messenger Isa (peace be upon him), one of the five great resolute messengers (ulu'l-azm), {she withdrew from her family to an eastern place}, meaning she separated herself from them and moved away, going to the east of the Sacred Sanctuary.

Al-Suddi said: because of menstruation that came upon her. Other reasons have also been given. Abu Kudayna reported from Qabus ibn Abi Zibyan, from his father, from Ibn Abbas, who said: the People of the Book had been prescribed prayer toward the House and pilgrimage to it, and nothing turned them away from it except a saying of your Lord: {she withdrew from her family to an eastern place}, meaning: Maryam went out to an eastern place, so they began to pray toward the rising of the sun. Reported by Ibn Abi Hatim and Ibn Jarir.

Ibn Jarir also said: [chain] Ishaq ibn Shahin told us, Khalid ibn Abdullah told us, from Dawud, from Amir, from Ibn Abbas, who said: I know, of all God's creation, why the Christians took the east as their qibla, because of God's saying, the Exalted: {she withdrew from her family to an eastern place}, and they took the birthplace of Isa as their qibla.

Qatada said: {an eastern place} means far off and secluded.

Muhammad ibn Ishaq said: she went with her water jug to draw water.

Nawf al-Bikali said: she took for herself a dwelling in which to worship. God knows best.

His saying: {So she took, apart from them, a veil}, meaning she concealed and hid herself from them. So God the Exalted sent to her Jibril (peace be upon him): {and he appeared to her in the form of a well-proportioned man}, meaning in the form of a complete, perfect human being.

Mujahid, al-Dahhak, Qatada, Ibn Jurayj, Wahb ibn Munabbih, and al-Suddi said, regarding His saying {So We sent to her Our spirit}: meaning Jibril (peace be upon him).

What they said is the apparent meaning of the Qur'an, for God the Exalted said in another verse: {The trustworthy Spirit brought it down upon your heart, that you may be among the warners} [al-Shu'ara: 193-194].

Abu Ja'far al-Razi reported from al-Rabi ibn Anas, from Abu al-Aliya, from Ubayy ibn Ka'b, who said: the spirit of Isa (peace be upon him) is among the spirits from whom the covenant was taken in the time of Adam, and it is that which appeared to her as a well-proportioned man, meaning the spirit of Isa, so she conceived him who spoke to her and entered into her mouth.

This is exceedingly strange and objectionable, and it appears to be an Israelite report (isra'iliyyat).

{She said, "Indeed I seek refuge in the Most Merciful from you, if you are God-fearing"}, meaning: when the angel appeared to her in the form of a human being, while she was in a secluded place with a veil between herself and her people, she feared him and thought he intended to take her by force. So she said: {Indeed I seek refuge in the Most Merciful from you, if you are God-fearing}, meaning: if you fear God. This was a reminder to him of God. This is the prescribed manner of repelling harm, that one proceed by the easiest means first, so she first frightened him with mention of God, Mighty and Majestic.

Ibn Jarir said: [chain] Abu Kurayb told me, Abu Bakr told us, from Asim, who said: Abu Wa'il said, mentioning the story of Maryam: she indeed knew that the God-fearing person possesses restraint (nuhya), when she said: {Indeed I seek refuge in the Most Merciful from you, if you are God-fearing. He said, "I am only the messenger of your Lord"}, meaning: the angel replied to her, removing the fear she had for herself, saying: I am not what you suppose, rather I am the messenger of your Lord, meaning He sent me to you. It is said that when she mentioned the Most Merciful, Jibril trembled in awe and returned to his true form, and said: "I am only the messenger of your Lord, that I may bestow upon you a pure boy."

[This is how Abu Amr ibn al-Ala, one of the well-known reciters, read it. The others read: {that I (myself) may bestow upon you a pure boy}]. Both readings have a good aspect and a sound meaning, and each necessarily implies the other.

{She said, "How can I have a boy while no man has touched me, and I have not been unchaste?"}, meaning: Maryam was astonished at this and said: how can I have a boy, meaning, in what manner will this boy come to be from me, when I have no husband, and unchastity cannot be imagined of me. This is why she said: {while no man has touched me, and I have not been unchaste}. Al-baghiyy is the fornicatress; this is why it comes in the hadith that the wage of the baghiyy (a prostitute's earnings) is forbidden.

{He said, "Thus it is. Your Lord says, 'It is easy for Me'"}, meaning: the angel replied to her regarding what she had asked: God has indeed said that a boy will come to be from you, even though you have no husband and no indecency is found in you, for He is capable of whatever He wills. This is why He said: {and that We may make him a sign for people}, meaning a proof and a sign for people of the power of their Originator and Creator, who diversified in their creation. He created their father Adam neither from a male nor a female, He created Hawwa (Eve) from a male without a female, and He created the rest of the offspring from a male and a female, except Isa, whom He brought into being from a female without a male. Thus the fourfold division was completed, demonstrating the completeness of His power and the greatness of His dominion. There is no god besides Him and no lord other than Him.

His saying: {and a mercy from Us}, meaning: We make this boy a mercy from God, a prophet among the prophets calling to the worship of God the Exalted and His oneness, as God the Exalted said in another verse: {When the angels said, "O Maryam, indeed God gives you glad tidings of a word from Him, whose name is the Messiah, Isa son of Maryam, honored in this world and the Hereafter, and among those brought near. He will speak to the people in the cradle and in maturity, and he is among the righteous"} [Al Imran: 45-46], meaning: he calls to the worship of God his Lord both in his cradle and in his maturity.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] my father told us, Abd al-Rahim ibn Ibrahim, Duhaym, told us, Marwan told us, al-Ala ibn al-Harith al-Kufi told us, from Mujahid, who said: Maryam (peace be upon her) said: when I was alone, Isa would speak to me and converse with me while he was in my womb, and when I was with people he would glorify God and say "God is greater" (takbir) in my womb.

His saying: {And it was a matter decreed}: it is possible that this is from the speech of Jibril to Maryam, informing her that this matter was predetermined in God's knowledge, decree, and will. It is also possible that this is a report from God the Exalted to His messenger Muhammad ﷺ, and that He alluded by this to the breathing of the spirit into her private part, as God the Exalted said: {And Maryam, daughter of Imran, who guarded her chastity, so We breathed into it of Our Spirit} [al-Tahrim: 12], and He said: {And she who guarded her chastity, so We breathed into her of Our Spirit} [al-Anbiya: 91].

Muhammad ibn Ishaq said: {And it was a matter decreed}, meaning: God had determined this matter, and there was no avoiding it. Ibn Jarir also chose this view in his tafsir, and related no other view. God knows best.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

لَمَّا ذَكَرَ تَعَالَى قِصَّةَ زَكَرِيَّا، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، وَأَنَّهُ أَوْجَدَ مِنْهُ، فِي حَالِ كِبَرِهِ وَعُقْمِ زَوْجَتِهِ، وَلَدًا زَكِيًّا طَاهِرًا مُبَارَكًا -عَطَفَ بِذِكْرِ قِصَّةِ مَرْيَمَ فِي إِيجَادِهِ وَلَدَهَا عِيسَى، عَلَيْهِمَا السَّلَامُ، مِنْهَا مِنْ غَيْرِ أَبٍ، فَإِنَّ بَيْنَ الْقِصَّتَيْنِ مُنَاسَبَةً وَمُشَابَهَةً ؛ وَلِهَذَا ذَكَرَهُمَا فِي آلِ عِمْرَانَ وَهَاهُنَا وَفِي سُورَةِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ، يُقْرِنُ بَيْنَ الْقِصَّتَيْنِ لِتَقَارُبِ مَا بَيْنَهُمَا فِي الْمَعْنَى، لِيَدُلَّ عِبَادَهُ عَلَى قُدْرَتِهِ وعظمة سلطانه، وأنه على ما يشاء قَادِرٌ ، فَقَالَ: ﴿وَاذْكُرْ فِي الْكِتَابِ مَرْيَمَ﴾ وَهِيَ مَرْيَمُ بِنْتُ عِمْرَانَ، مِنْ سُلَالَةِ دَاوُدَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، وَكَانَتْ مِنْ بَيْتٍ طَاهِرٍ طَيِّبٍ فِي بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ. وَقَدْ ذَكَرَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى قِصَّةَ وِلَادَةِ أُمِّهَا لَهَا فِي "آلِ عِمْرَانَ"، وَأَنَّهَا نَذَرَتْهَا مُحَرَّرَةً، أَيْ: تَخْدُمُ مَسْجِدَ بَيْتِ الْمَقْدِسِ، وَكَانُوا يَتَقَرَّبُونَ بِذَلِكَ، ﴿فَتَقَبَّلَهَا رَبُّهَا بِقَبُولٍ حَسَنٍ وَأَنْبَتَهَا نَبَاتًا حَسَنًا﴾ [آلِ عِمْرَانَ: ٣٧] وَنَشَأَتْ فِي بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ نَشْأَةً عَظِيمَةً، فَكَانَتْ إِحْدَى الْعَابِدَاتِ النَّاسِكَاتِ الْمَشْهُورَاتِ بِالْعِبَادَةِ الْعَظِيمَةِ وَالتَّبَتُّلِ وَالدُّءُوبِ، وَكَانَتْ فِي كَفَالَةِ زَوْجِ أُخْتِهَا -وَقِيلَ: خَالَتِهَا-زَكَرِيَّا نَبِيِّ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ إِذْ ذَاكَ وَعَظِيمِهِمُ، الَّذِي يَرْجِعُونَ إِلَيْهِ فِي دِينِهِمْ. وَرَأَى لَهَا زَكَرِيَّا مِنَ الْكَرَامَاتِ الْهَائِلَةِ مَا بَهَرَهُ ﴿كُلَّمَا دَخَلَ عَلَيْهَا زَكَرِيَّا الْمِحْرَابَ وَجَدَ عِنْدَهَا رِزْقًا قَالَ يَا مَرْيَمُ أَنَّى لَكِ هَذَا قَالَتْ هُوَ مِنْ عِنْدِ اللَّهِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَرْزُقُ مَنْ يَشَاءُ بِغَيْرِ حِسَابٍ﴾ [آلِ عِمْرَانَ: ٣٧] فَذُكِرَ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَجِدُ عِنْدَهَا ثَمَرَ الشِّتَاءِ فِي الصَّيْفِ وَثَمَرَ الصَّيْفِ فِي الشِّتَاءِ، كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ بَيَانُهُ فِي "آلِ عِمْرَانَ". فَلَمَّا أَرَادَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى -وَلَهُ الْحِكْمَةُ وَالْحُجَّةُ الْبَالِغَةُ-أَنْ يُوجد مِنْهَا عَبْدَهُ وَرَسُولَهُ عِيسَى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، أَحَدَ الرُّسُلِ أُولِي الْعَزْمِ الْخَمْسَةِ الْعِظَامِ، ﴿انْتَبَذَتْ مِنْ أَهْلِهَا مَكَانًا شَرْقِيًّا﴾ أَيِ: اعْتَزَلَتْهُمْ وَتَنَحَّتْ عَنْهُمْ، وَذَهَبَتْ إِلَى شَرْقِ الْمَسْجِدِ الْمُقَدَّسِ.

قَالَ السُّدِّيُّ: لِحَيْضٍ أَصَابَهَا. وَقِيلَ لِغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ. قَالَ أَبُو كُدَيْنَة، عَنْ قَابُوسُ بْنُ أَبِي ظِبْيان، عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: إِنَّ أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ كُتِبَ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ وَالْحَجُّ إِلَيْهِ، وَمَا صَرَفَهُمْ عَنْهُ إِلَّا قِيلُ رَبِّكَ: ﴿انْتَبَذَتْ مِنْ أَهْلِهَا مَكَانًا شَرْقِيًّا﴾ قَالَ: خَرَجَتْ مَرْيَمُ مَكَانًا شَرْقِيًّا، فَصَلُّوا قِبَلَ مَطْلِعِ الشَّمْسِ. رَوَاهُ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ، وَابْنُ جَرِيرٍ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ أَيْضًا: حَدَّثَنَا إِسْحَاقُ بْنُ شَاهِينَ، حَدَّثَنَا خَالِدُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنْ دَاوُدَ، عَنْ عَامِرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: إِنِّي لَأَعْلَمُ خَلْقِ اللَّهِ لِأَيِّ شَيْءٍ اتَّخَذَتِ النَّصَارَى الْمَشْرِقَ قِبْلَةً؛ لِقَوْلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى ﴿انْتَبَذَتْ مِنْ أَهْلِهَا مَكَانًا شَرْقِيًّا﴾ وَاتَّخَذُوا مِيلَادَ عِيسَى قِبْلَةً 

وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ: ﴿مَكَانًا شَرْقِيًّا﴾ شَاسِعًا مُتَنَحِّيًا.

وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ: ذَهَبَتْ بِقُلَّتِهَا تَسْتَقِي [مِنَ] الْمَاءِ.

وَقَالَ نَوْف البِكَالي: اتَّخَذَتْ لَهَا مَنْزِلًا تَتَعَبَّدُ فِيهِ. فَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿فَاتَّخَذَتْ مِنْ دُونِهِمْ حِجَابًا﴾ أَيِ: اسْتَتَرَتْ مِنْهُمْ وَتَوَارَتْ، فَأَرْسَلَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى إِلَيْهَا جِبْرِيلَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ ﴿فَتَمَثَّلَ لَهَا بَشَرًا سَوِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: عَلَى صُورَةِ إِنْسَانٍ تَامٍّ كَامِلٍ.

قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ، وَالضَّحَّاكُ، وقَتَادَةُ، وَابْنُ جُرَيْج وَوَهْبُ بْنُ مُنَبِّه، والسُّدِّي، فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿فَأَرْسَلْنَا إِلَيْهَا رُوحَنَا﴾ يعني: جبريل، عليه السلام.

وَهَذَا الَّذِي قَالُوهُ هُوَ ظَاهِرُ الْقُرْآنِ فَإِنَّهُ تَعَالَى قَدْ قَالَ فِي الْآيَةِ الْأُخْرَى: ﴿نزلَ بِهِ الرُّوحُ الأمِينُ عَلَى قَلْبِكَ لِتَكُونَ مِنَ الْمُنْذِرِينَ﴾ [الشُّعَرَاءِ: ١٩٣، ١٩٤] .

وَقَالَ أَبُو جَعْفَرٍ الرَّازِيُّ ، عَنِ الرَّبِيعِ بْنِ أَنَسٍ، عَنْ أَبِي الْعَالِيَةِ، عَنْ أُبَيِّ بْنِ كَعْبٍ قَالَ: إِنَّ رُوحَ عِيسَى، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، مِنْ جُمْلَةِ الْأَرْوَاحِ الَّتِي أُخِذَ عَلَيْهَا الْعَهْدُ فِي زَمَانِ آدَمَ، وَهُوَ الَّذِي تَمَثَّلَ لَهَا بَشَرًا سَوِيًّا، أَيْ: رُوحُ عِيسَى، فَحَمَلَتِ الَّذِي خَاطَبَهَا وَحَلَّ فِي فِيهَا.

وَهَذَا فِي غَايَةِ الْغَرَابَةِ وَالنَّكَارَةِ، وَكَأَنَّهُ إِسْرَائِيلِيٌّ.

﴿قَالَتْ إِنِّي أَعُوذُ بِالرَّحْمَنِ مِنْكَ إِنْ كُنْتَ تَقِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: لَمَّا تَبَدى لَهَا الْمَلَكُ فِي صُورَةِ بَشَرٍ، وَهِيَ فِي مَكَانٍ مُنْفَرِدٍ وَبَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ قَوْمِهَا حِجَابٌ، خَافَتْهُ وَظَنَّتْ أَنَّهُ يُرِيدُهَا عَلَى نَفْسِهَا، فَقَالَتْ: ﴿إِنِّي أَعُوذُ بِالرَّحْمَنِ مِنْكَ إِنْ كُنْتَ تَقِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: إِنْ كُنْتَ تَخَافُ اللَّهَ. تَذْكِيرٌ لَهُ بِاللَّهِ، وَهَذَا هُوَ الْمَشْرُوعُ فِي الدَّفْعِ أَنْ يَكُونَ بِالْأَسْهَلِ فَالْأَسْهَلِ، فَخَوَّفَتْهُ أَوَّلًا بِاللَّهِ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ.

قَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنِي أَبُو كُرَيْب، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو بَكْرٍ، عَنْ عَاصِمٍ قَالَ: قَالَ أَبُو وَائِلٍ -وَذَكَرَ قِصَّةَ مَرْيَمَ-فَقَالَ: قَدْ عَلِمَتْ أَنَّ التَّقِيَّ ذُو نُهْيَة حِينَ قَالَتْ: ﴿إِنِّي أَعُوذُ بِالرَّحْمَنِ مِنْكَ إِنْ كُنْتَ تَقِيًّا قَالَ إِنَّمَا أَنَا رَسُولُ رَبِّكِ﴾ أَيْ: فَقَالَ لَهَا الْمَلَكُ مُجِيبًا لَهَا وَمُزِيلًا مَا حَصَلَ عِنْدَهَا مِنَ الْخَوْفِ عَلَى نَفْسِهَا: لَسْتُ مِمَّا تَظُنِّينَ، وَلَكِنِّي رَسُولُ رَبِّكِ، أَيْ: بَعَثَنِي إِلَيْكِ، وَيُقَالُ: إِنَّهَا لَمَّا ذَكَرَتِ الرَّحْمَنَ انْتَفَضَ جِبْرِيلُ فَرَقًا وَعَادَ إِلَى هَيْئَتِهِ وَقَالَ: "إِنَّمَا أَنَا رَسُولُ رَبِّكِ لِيَهَبَ لَكِ غُلَامًا زَكِيًّا".

[هَكَذَا قَرَأَ أَبُو عَمْرِو بْنُ الْعَلَاءِ أَحَدُ مَشْهُورِي الْقُرَّاءِ. وَقَرَأَ الْآخَرُونَ: ﴿لأهَبَ لَكِ غُلامًا زَكِيًّا﴾ ] وَكِلَا الْقِرَاءَتَيْنِ لَهُ وَجْهٌ حَسَنٌ، وَمَعْنًى صَحِيحٌ، وَكُلٌّ تَسْتَلْزِمُ الْأُخْرَى.

﴿قَالَتْ أَنَّى يَكُونُ لِي غُلامٌ وَلَمْ يَمْسَسْنِي بَشَرٌ وَلَم أَكُ بَغِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: فَتَعَجَّبَتْ مَرْيَمُ مِنْ هَذَا وَقَالَتْ: كَيْفَ يَكُونُ لِي غُلَامٌ؟ أَيْ: عَلَى أَيِّ صِفَةٍ يُوجَدُ هَذَا الْغُلَامُ مِنِّي، وَلَسْتُ بِذَاتِ زَوْجٍ، وَلَا يُتَصَوَّرُ مِنِّي الْفُجُورُ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَتْ: ﴿وَلَمْ يَمْسَسْنِي بَشَرٌ وَلَمْ أَكُ بَغِيًّا﴾ وَالْبَغِيُّ: هِيَ الزَّانِيَةُ؛ وَلِهَذَا جَاءَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ نُهِيَ عَنْ مَهْرِ الْبَغِيِّ.

﴿قَالَ كَذَلِكَ قَالَ رَبُّكَ هُوَ عَلَيَّ هَيِّنٌ﴾ أَيْ: فَقَالَ لَهَا الْمَلَكُ مُجِيبًا لَهَا عَمَّا سَأَلَتْ: إِنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ قَالَ: إِنَّهُ سَيُوجَدُ مِنْكِ غُلَامًا، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَكِ بَعْلٌ وَلَا تُوجَدُ مِنْكِ فَاحِشَةٌ، فَإِنَّهُ عَلَى مَا يَشَاءُ قَادِرٌ ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿وَلِنَجْعَلَهُ آيَةً لِلنَّاسِ﴾ أَيْ: دَلَالَةً وَعَلَامَةً لِلنَّاسِ عَلَى قُدْرَةِ بَارِئِهِمْ وَخَالِقِهِمُ، الَّذِي نَوَّعَ فِي خَلْقِهِمْ، فَخَلَقَ أَبَاهُمْ آدَمَ مِنْ غَيْرِ ذَكَرٍ وَلَا أُنْثَى، وَخَلَقَ حَوَّاءَ مِنْ ذَكَرٍ بِلَا أُنْثَى، وَخَلَقَ بَقِيَّةَ الذُّرِّيَّةِ مَنْ ذَكَرٍ وَأُنْثَى، إِلَّا عِيسَى فَإِنَّهُ أَوْجَدَهُ مِنْ أُنْثَى بِلَا ذَكَرٍ، فَتَمَّتِ الْقِسْمَةُ الرُّبَاعِيَّةُ الدَّالَّةُ عَلَى كَمَالِ قُدْرَتِهِ وَعَظِيمِ سُلْطَانِهِ فَلَا إِلَهَ غَيْرُهُ وَلَا رَبَّ سِوَاهُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَرَحْمَةً مِنَّا﴾ أَيْ وَنَجْعَلُ هَذَا الْغُلَامَ رَحْمَةً مِنَ اللَّهِ نَبِيًّا من الأنبياء يدعو إلى عبادة اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَتَوْحِيدِهِ، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي الْآيَةِ الْأُخْرَى: ﴿إِذْ قَالَتِ الْمَلائِكَةُ يَا مَرْيَمُ إِنَّ اللَّهَ يُبَشِّرُكِ بِكَلِمَةٍ مِنْهُ اسْمُهُ الْمَسِيحُ عِيسَى ابْنُ مَرْيَمَ وَجِيهًا فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالآخِرَةِ وَمِنَ الْمُقَرَّبِينَ وَيُكَلِّمُ النَّاسَ فِي الْمَهْدِ وَكَهْلا وَمِنَ الصَّالِحِينَ﴾ [آلِ عِمْرَانَ: ٤٥، ٤٦] أَيْ: يَدْعُو إِلَى عِبَادَةِ اللَّهِ رَبِّهِ فِي مَهْدِهِ وَكُهُولَتِهِ.

قَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبِي، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّحِيمِ بْنُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ -دُحَيْم-حَدَّثَنَا مَرْوَانُ، حَدَّثَنَا الْعَلَاءُ بْنُ الْحَارِثِ الْكُوفِيُّ، عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ قَالَ: قَالَتْ مَرْيَمُ، عَلَيْهَا السَّلَامُ: كُنْتُ إِذَا خَلَوْتُ حَدَّثَنِي عِيسَى وَكَلَّمَنِي وَهُوَ فِي بَطْنِي وَإِذَا كُنْتُ مَعَ النَّاسِ سَبَّحَ فِي بَطْنِي وَكَبَّرَ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَكَانَ أَمْرًا مَقْضِيًّا﴾ يُحْتَمَلُ أَنَّ هَذَا مِنْ كَلَامِ جِبْرِيلَ لِمَرْيَمَ، يُخْبِرُهَا أَنَّ هَذَا أَمْرٌ مُقَدَّرٌ فِي عِلْمِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَقَدَرِهُ وَمَشِيئَتِهِ. وَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مِنْ خَبَرِ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى لِرَسُولِهِ مُحَمَّدٍ ﷺ وَأَنَّهُ كَنَّى بِهَذَا عَنِ النَّفْخِ فِي فَرْجِهَا، كما قال تَعَالَى: ﴿وَمَرْيَمَ ابْنَتَ عِمْرَانَ الَّتِي أَحْصَنَتْ فَرْجَهَا فَنَفَخْنَا فِيهِ مِنْ رُوحِنَا﴾ [التَّحْرِيمِ: ١٢] وَقَالَ ﴿وَالَّتِي أَحْصَنَتْ فَرْجَهَا فَنَفَخْنَا فِيهَا مِنْ رُوحِنَا﴾ [الْأَنْبِيَاءِ: ٩١]

قَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ: ﴿وَكَانَ أَمْرًا مَقْضِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: أَنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ عَزَمَ عَلَى هَذَا، فَلَيْسَ مِنْهُ بُدٌّ، وَاخْتَارَ هَذَا أَيْضًا ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ فِي تَفْسِيرِهِ، وَلَمْ يَحْكِ غَيْرَهُ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

---

## 19:22-23 — verses 22-23 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Most High says, informing us about Mary, that when Gabriel said to her, on behalf of God the Most High, what he said, she submitted to God's decree, the Most High. A number of the scholars of the early generations mentioned that the angel, namely Gabriel (peace be upon him), at that point blew into the opening of her garment, and the breath descended until it entered the womb, and she conceived the child by the permission of God the Most High. When she conceived him, she was greatly distressed by it and did not know what she would say to the people, for she knew that people would not believe her in what she would tell them. However, she disclosed her secret and mentioned her matter to her kinswoman, the wife of Zechariah (Zakariyya).

That was because Zechariah, peace be upon him, had asked God for a child, and his prayer was answered, so his wife conceived. Mary came to visit her, and she rose to her and embraced her, and said: "Mary, do you know that I am pregnant?" Mary said to her: "And do you also know that I am pregnant?" And she told her of her situation and what had happened to her. They were a household of faith and belief. Thereafter, whenever the wife of Zechariah faced Mary, she would find that which was in her own womb prostrating to that which was in Mary's womb, meaning honoring it and submitting to it, for prostration in their religious law upon greeting was a legislated practice, just as Joseph's parents and brothers prostrated to him, and just as God commanded the angels to prostrate to Adam, peace be upon him. But it has been forbidden in our religious law, in completion of the glorification of the majesty of the Lord, the Most High.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Ali ibn al-Husayn said: it was read to al-Harith ibn Miskin while I was listening, he said: Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Qasim informed us, he said: Malik, may God have mercy on him, said: it has reached me that Jesus son of Mary and John (Yahya) son of Zechariah were maternal cousins, and their conception occurred together at the same time. It has reached me that the mother of John said to Mary: "I sense that what is in my womb prostrates to what is in your womb." Malik said: I consider that to be due to the superiority of Jesus, peace be upon him, because God made him give life to the dead and heal the blind and the leper.

The commentators then differed regarding the duration of Mary's pregnancy with Jesus, peace be upon him. The well-known view among the majority is that she carried him for nine months. Ikrimah said: eight months, and he said: that is why a child born at eight months does not survive.

Ibn Jurayj said: al-Mughirah ibn Uthman ibn Abdullah al-Thaqafi informed me, he heard Ibn Abbas being asked about Mary's pregnancy, and he said: it was nothing but that she conceived and then gave birth.

This is gharib (a singular report), and it seems he derived it from the apparent sense of God's saying: {So she conceived him, and she withdrew with him to a remote place. Then the pains of childbirth drove her to the trunk of a palm tree.} The letter "fa" (then/so), even though it indicates sequence, the sequencing of each thing is according to its own nature, just as God the Most High says: {And indeed We created man from an extract of clay. Then We made him a drop of fluid in a safe lodging. Then We made the drop into a clot, then We made the clot into a lump of flesh, then We made the lump of flesh into bones} [al-Mu'minun: 12-14]. This "fa" indicates sequence according to its own nature. It is established in the two authentic collections (al-Sahihayn) that between each of these two stages there are forty days. And God the Most High says: {Do you not see that God sends down water from the sky, and the earth becomes green} [al-Hajj: 63]. So the well-known and apparent view, and God is capable of all things, is that she carried him just as women carry their children.

For this reason, when the signs of pregnancy appeared on her, and there was with her in the sanctuary a righteous man among her relatives who served with her in the Holy House (Bayt al-Maqdis), called Joseph the Carpenter, when he saw the heaviness and size of her belly, he found that troubling regarding her matter. Then what he knew of her innocence, purity, religion and devotion turned him away from that suspicion. Then he reflected on her condition, and the matter kept circulating in his thoughts, and he could not turn it away from himself, so he pressed himself to hint at it in speech, and said: "O Mary, I am going to ask you about a matter, so do not be hasty with me." She said: "What is it?" He said: "Can a tree ever grow without a seed? Can a crop grow without a seed being sown? Can a child be born without a father?" She said: "Yes," having understood what he was alluding to. "As for your saying, 'Can a tree grow without a seed and a crop without a seed being sown,' God created trees and crops the first time He created them without seed and without sowing. And as for whether a created being can come about without a father, God created Adam without a father and without a mother." So he believed her, and accepted her situation as it was.

When Mary sensed that her people suspected her of impropriety, she withdrew from them to a remote place, meaning distant and far from them, so that she would not see them nor they see her.

Muhammad ibn Ishaq said: When she had conceived him and her time was complete and she returned, her menstrual blood ceased, and she was afflicted with what afflicts a pregnant woman carrying a child, such as weariness, tenderness, and change of complexion, until her tongue could no longer hold back speech. Nothing entered upon any household like what entered upon the household of Zechariah, and the news spread among the Children of Israel, and they said: "Her companion is none other than Joseph," for there had been no one else with her in the sanctuary but him. She hid herself from the people and took a veil between herself and them, so that no one would see her and she would not see them.

His saying: {Then the pains of childbirth drove her to the trunk of a palm tree} means: the labor pains compelled and forced her to the trunk of the palm tree, which was a palm tree in the place to which she had withdrawn.

They differed regarding it. Al-Suddi said: it was to the east of her prayer niche (mihrab) where she used to pray, in the Holy House.

Wahb ibn Munabbih said: she went fleeing, and when she was between the Levant (al-Sham) and the lands of Egypt, the labor pains struck her. In another report from Wahb: that occurred eight miles from the Holy House, in a village there called "Bethlehem" (Bayt Lahm).

I say: it has already been mentioned in the hadith of the Night Journey (al-Isra), by the report of al-Nasa'i from Anas, may God be pleased with him, and by al-Bayhaqi from Shaddad ibn Aws, may God be pleased with him, that this occurred at Bethlehem. God knows best. This is the well-known account which people have transmitted one from another, and the Christians have no doubt about it, that it was at Bethlehem, and people have received this account. It has been reported in hadith, if it is authentic.

His saying, the Most High, informing us of her: {She said, "Would that I had died before this, and had been a thing forgotten, utterly forgotten!"} contains proof that it is permissible to wish for death at a time of trial (fitnah), for she knew that she would be tested and tried by this newborn, whose situation people would not accept as sound, and would not believe her account regarding it. And after having been among them a devout worshipper and ascetic, she would become, in their assumption, an adulteress and fornicator. So she said: {Would that I had died before this,} meaning before this state, {and had been a thing forgotten, utterly forgotten,} meaning: had never been created and had not been anything at all. This was said by Ibn Abbas.

Al-Suddi said: she said this while in the pangs of labor, out of shyness before the people: "Would that I had died before this distress that I am in, and this sorrow at giving birth to a child without a husband." {And had been a thing forgotten, utterly forgotten,} meaning: forgotten and its being sought after abandoned, like the rags of menstruation when thrown away and discarded, no longer sought after or mentioned. And likewise everything that is forgotten and abandoned is called "nasiyy" (a forgotten thing).

Qatadah said: {and had been a thing forgotten, utterly forgotten} means: something not known, not mentioned, and it is not known who I am.

Al-Rabi ibn Anas said: {and had been a thing forgotten, utterly forgotten} refers to a miscarriage.

Ibn Zayd said: I had never been anything at all.

We have already presented, previously, the hadiths indicating the prohibition of wishing for death, except at a time of trial (fitnah), at the discussion of His saying: {Take my soul in submission to You, and join me with the righteous} [Yusuf: 101].

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى مُخْبِرًا عَنْ مَرْيَمَ أَنَّهَا لَمَّا قَالَ لَهَا جِبْرِيلُ عَنِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى مَا قَالَ، إِنَّهَا اسْتَسْلَمَتْ لِقَضَاءِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فَذَكَرَ غَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عُلَمَاءِ السَّلَفِ أَنَّ الْمَلَكَ -وَهُوَ جِبْرِيلُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ-عِنْدَ ذَلِكَ نَفَخَ فِي جَيْبِ دِرْعِهَا، فَنَزَلَتِ النَّفْخَةُ حَتَّى وَلَجَتْ فِي الْفَرْجِ، فَحَمَلَتْ بِالْوَلَدِ بِإِذْنِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى. فَلَمَّا حَمَلَتْ بِهِ ضَاقَتْ ذَرْعًا بِهِ وَلَمْ تَدْرِ مَاذَا تَقُولُ لِلنَّاسِ، فَإِنَّهَا تَعْلَمُ أَنَّ النَّاسَ لَا يُصَدِّقُونَهَا فِيمَا تُخْبِرُهُمْ بِهِ، غَيْرَ أَنَّهَا أَفْشَتْ سِرَّهَا وَذَكَرَتْ أَمْرَهَا لِأُخْتِهَا امْرَأَةِ زَكَرِيَّا. وَذَلِكَ أَنَّ زَكَرِيَّا عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، كَانَ قَدْ سَأَلَ اللَّهَ الْوَلَدَ، فَأُجِيبَ إِلَى ذَلِكَ، فَحَمَلَتِ امْرَأَتُهُ، فَدَخَلَتْ عَلَيْهَا مَرْيَمُ فَقَامَتْ إِلَيْهَا فَاعْتَنَقَتْهَا، وَقَالَتْ: أَشَعَرْتِ يَا مَرْيَمُ أَنِّي حُبْلَى؟ فَقَالَتْ لَهَا مَرْيَمُ: وَهَلْ عَلِمْتِ أَيْضًا أَنِّي حُبْلَى؟ وَذَكَرَتْ لَهَا شَأْنَهَا وَمَا كَانَ مِنْ خَبَرِهَا وَكَانُوا بَيْتَ إِيمَانٍ وَتَصْدِيقٍ، ثُمَّ كَانَتِ امْرَأَةُ زَكَرِيَّا بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ إِذَا وَاجَهَتْ مَرْيَمَ تَجِدُ الَّذِي فِي جَوْفِهَا يَسْجُدُ لِلَّذِي فِي بَطْنِ مَرْيَمَ، أَيْ: يُعَظِّمُهُ وَيَخْضَعُ لَهُ، فَإِنَّ السُّجُودَ كَانَ فِي مِلَّتِهِمْ عِنْدَ السَّلَامِ مَشْرُوعًا، كَمَا سَجَدَ لِيُوسُفَ أَبَوَاهُ وَإِخْوَتُهُ، وَكَمَا أَمَرَ اللَّهُ الْمَلَائِكَةَ أَنْ تَسْجُدَ لِآدَمَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، وَلَكِنْ حُرِّمَ فِي مِلَّتِنَا هَذِهِ تَكْمِيلًا لِتَعْظِيمِ جَلَالِ الرَّبِّ تَعَالَى.

قَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا عَلِيُّ بْنُ الْحُسَيْنِ قَالَ: قُرِئَ عَلَى الْحَارِثِ بْنِ مِسْكِينٍ وَأَنَا أَسْمَعُ، قَالَ: أَخْبَرَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ الْقَاسِمِ قَالَ: قَالَ مَالِكٌ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: بَلَغَنِي أَنَّ عِيسَى ابْنَ مَرْيَمَ وَيَحْيَى بْنَ زَكَرِيَّا ابْنَا خَالَةٍ، وَكَانَ حَمْلُهُمَا جَمِيعًا مَعًا، فَبَلَغَنِي أَنَّ أُمَّ يَحْيَى قَالَتْ لِمَرْيَمَ: إِنِّي أَرَى أَنَّ مَا فِي بَطْنِي يَسْجُدُ لِمَا فِي بَطْنِكِ. قَالَ مَالِكٌ: أَرَى ذَلِكَ لِتَفْضِيلِ عِيسَى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ؛ لِأَنَّ اللَّهَ جَعَلَهُ يُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى وَيُبْرِئُ الْأَكْمَهَ وَالْأَبْرَصَ.

ثُمَّ اخْتَلَفَ الْمُفَسِّرُونَ فِي مُدَّةِ حَمْلِ عِيسَى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَالْمَشْهُورُ عَنِ الْجُمْهُورِ أَنَّهَا حَمَلَتْ بِهِ تِسْعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ. وَقَالَ عِكْرِمَةُ: ثَمَانِيَةُ أَشْهُرٍ -قَالَ: وَلِهَذَا لَا يَعِيشُ وَلَدٌ لِثَمَانِيَةِ أَشْهُرٍ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْج: أَخْبَرَنِي الْمُغِيرَةُ بْنُ عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الثَّقَفِيُّ، سَمِعَ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ وَسُئِلَ عَنْ حَبَل مَرْيَمَ، قَالَ: لَمْ يَكُنْ إِلَّا أَنْ حَمَلَتْ فَوَضَعَتْ .

وَهَذَا غَرِيبٌ، وَكَأَنَّهُ أَخَذَهُ مِنْ ظَاهِرِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَحَمَلَتْهُ فَانْتَبَذَتْ بِهِ مَكَانًا قَصِيًّا فَأَجَاءَهَا الْمَخَاضُ إِلَى جِذْعِ النَّخْلَةِ﴾ فَالْفَاءُ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ لِلتَّعْقِيبِ، وَلَكِنَّ تَعْقِيبَ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ بِحَسْبِهِ، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا الإنْسَانَ مِنْ سُلالَةٍ مِنْ طِينٍ ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَاهُ نُطْفَةً فِي قَرَارٍ مَكِينٍ ثُمَّ خَلَقْنَا النُّطْفَةَ عَلَقَةً فَخَلَقْنَا الْعَلَقَةَ مُضْغَةً فَخَلَقْنَا الْمُضْغَةَ عِظَامًا﴾ [الْمُؤْمِنُونَ: ١٢ -١٤] فَهَذِهِ الْفَاءُ لِلتَّعْقِيبِ بِحَسْبِهَا. وَقَدْ ثَبَتَ فِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ: أَنَّ بَيْنَ كُلِّ صِفَتَيْنِ أَرْبَعِينَ يَوْمًا وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ أَنزلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً فَتُصْبِحُ الأرْضُ مُخْضَرَّةً﴾ [الْحَجِّ: ٦٣] فَالْمَشْهُورُ الظَّاهِرُ -وَاللَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ-أَنَّهَا حَمَلَتْ بِهِ كَمَا تَحْمِلُ النِّسَاءُ بِأَوْلَادِهِنَّ؛ وَلِهَذَا لَمَّا ظَهَرَتْ مَخَايِلُ الْحَمْلِ عَلَيْهَا وَكَانَ مَعَهَا فِي الْمَسْجِدِ رَجُلٌ صَالِحٌ مِنْ قَرَابَاتِهَا يَخْدِمُ مَعَهَا الْبَيْتَ الْمُقَدَّسَ، يُقَالُ لَهُ: يُوسُفُ النَّجَّارُ، فَلَمَّا رَأَى ثِقَلَ بَطْنِهَا وَكِبَرَهُ، أَنْكَرَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ أَمْرِهَا، ثُمَّ صَرَفَهُ مَا يَعْلَمُ مِنْ بَرَاءَتِهَا وَنَزَاهَتِهَا وَدِينِهَا وَعِبَادَتِهَا، ثُمَّ تَأَمَّلَ مَا هِيَ فِيهِ، فَجَعَلَ أَمْرُهَا يَجُوسُ فِي فِكْرِهِ، لَا يَسْتَطِيعُ صَرْفَهُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ، فَحَمَلَ نَفْسَهُ عَلَى أَنْ عَرَّضَ لَهَا فِي الْقَوْلِ، فَقَالَ: يَا مَرْيَمُ، إِنِّي سَائِلُكِ عَنْ أَمْرٍ فَلَا تَعْجَلِي عَلَيَّ. قَالَتْ: وَمَا هُوَ؟ قَالَ: هَلْ يَكُونُ قَطُّ شَجَرٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ حَبٍّ؟ وَهَلْ يَكُونُ زَرْعٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ بَذْرٍ؟ وَهَلْ يَكُونُ وَلَدٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَبٍ؟ فَقَالَتْ: نَعَمْ -فَهِمَتْ مَا أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ-أَمَّا قَوْلُكَ: "هَلْ يَكُونُ شَجَرٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ حَبٍّ وَزَرْعٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ بَذْرٍ؟ " فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ خَلَقَ الشَّجَرَ وَالزَّرْعَ أَوَّلَ مَا خَلَقَهُمَا مِنْ غَيْرِ حَبٍّ، وَلَا بَذْرٍ "وَهَلْ خَلْقٌ يَكُونُ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَبٍ؟ " فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ خَلَقَ آدَمَ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَبٍ وَلَا أُمٍّ. فَصَدَّقَهَا، وسلَّم لَهَا حَالَهَا.

وَلَمَّا اسْتَشْعَرَتْ مَرْيَمُ مِنْ قَوْمِهَا اتِّهَامَهَا بِالرِّيبَةِ، انْتَبَذَتْ مِنْهُمْ مَكَانًا قَصِيًّا، أَيْ: قَاصِيًا مِنْهُمْ بَعِيدًا عَنْهُمْ؛ لِئَلَّا تَرَاهُمْ وَلَا يَرَوْهَا.

قَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ: فَلَمَّا حَمَلَتْ بِهِ وَمَلَأَتْ قُلَّتَهَا وَرَجَعَتْ، اسْتَمْسَكَ عَنْهَا الدَّمُ وَأَصَابَهَا مَا يُصِيبُ الْحَامِلَ عَلَى الْوَلَدِ مِنَ الْوَصَبِ وَالتَّرَحُّمِ وَتَغَيُّرِ اللَّوْنِ، حَتَّى فَطَرَ لِسَانُهَا، فَمَا دَخَلَ عَلَى أَهْلِ بَيْتٍ مَا دَخَلَ عَلَى آلِ زَكَرِيَّا، وَشَاعَ الْحَدِيثُ فِي بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ، فَقَالُوا: "إِنَّمَا صَاحِبُهَا يُوسُفُ"، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ مَعَهَا فِي الْكَنِيسَةِ غَيْرُهُ، وَتَوَارَتْ مِنَ النَّاسِ، وَاتَّخَذَتْ مِنْ دونهم حجابًا، فلا يراها أحد ولا تَرَاهُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿فَأَجَاءَهَا الْمَخَاضُ إِلَى جِذْعِ النَّخْلَةِ﴾ [أَيْ: فَاضْطَرَّهَا وَأَلْجَأَهَا الطَّلْقُ إِلَى جِذْعِ النَّخْلَةِ] وَهِيَ نَخْلَةٌ فِي الْمَكَانِ الَّذِي تَنَحَّتْ إِلَيْهِ.

وَقَدِ اخْتَلَفُوا فِيهِ، فَقَالَ السُّدِّيُّ: كَانَ شَرْقِيَّ مِحْرَابِهَا الَّذِي تُصَلِّي فِيهِ مِنْ بَيْتِ الْمَقْدِسِ.

وَقَالَ وَهْبُ بْنُ مُنَبِّه: ذَهَبَتْ هَارِبَةً، فَلَمَّا كَانَتْ بَيْنَ الشَّامِ وَبِلَادِ مِصْرَ، ضَرَبَهَا الطَّلْقُ. وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ عَنْ وَهْبٍ: كَانَ ذَلِكَ عَلَى ثَمَانِيَةِ أَمْيَالٍ مِنْ بَيْتِ الْمَقْدِسِ، فِي قَرْيَةٍ هُنَاكَ يُقَالُ لَهَا: "بَيْتُ لَحْمٍ".

قُلْتُ: وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ فِي حَدِيثِ الْإِسْرَاءِ، مِنْ رِوَايَةِ النَّسَائِيِّ عَنْ أَنَسٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، وَالْبَيْهَقِيِّ عَنْ شدَّاد بْنِ أَوْسٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ: أَنَّ ذَلِكَ بِبَيْتِ لَحْمٍ، فَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ، وَهَذَا هُوَ الْمَشْهُورُ الَّذِي تَلَقَّاهُ النَّاسُ بَعْضُهُمْ عَنْ بَعْضٍ، وَلَا يَشُكُّ فِيهِ النَّصَارَى أَنَّهُ بِبَيْتِ لَحْمٍ، وَقَدْ تَلَقَّاهُ النَّاسُ. وَقَدْ وَرَدَ بِهِ الْحَدِيثُ إِنْ صَحَّ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى إِخْبَارًا عَنْهَا: ﴿قَالَتْ يَا لَيْتَنِي مِتُّ قَبْلَ هَذَا وَكُنْتُ نَسْيًا مَنْسِيًّا﴾ فِيهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى جَوَازِ تَمَنِّي الْمَوْتِ عِنْدَ الْفِتْنَةِ، فَإِنَّهَا عَرَفَتْ أَنَّهَا سَتُبْتَلَى وَتُمْتَحَنُ بِهَذَا الْمَوْلُودِ الَّذِي لَا يَحْمِلُ النَّاسُ أَمْرَهَا فِيهِ عَلَى السَّدَادِ، وَلَا يُصَدِّقُونَهَا فِي خَبَرِهَا، وَبَعْدَمَا كَانَتْ عِنْدَهُمْ عَابِدَةً نَاسِكَةً، تُصْبِحُ عِنْدَهُمْ فِيمَا يَظُنُّونَ عَاهِرَةً زَانِيَةً، فَقَالَتْ: ﴿يَا لَيْتَنِي مِتُّ قَبْلَ هَذَا﴾ أَي قَبْلَ هَذَا الْحَالِ، ﴿وَكُنْتُ نَسْيًا مَنْسِيًّا﴾ أَي لَمْ أُخْلَقْ وَلَمْ أَكُ شَيْئًا. قَالَهُ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ.

وَقَالَ السُّدِّيُّ: قَالَتْ وَهِيَ تَطْلِقُ مِنَ الْحَبَلِ -اسْتِحْيَاءً مِنَ النَّاسِ: يَا لَيْتَنِي مِتُّ قَبْلَ هَذَا الْكَرْبِ الَّذِي أَنَا فِيهِ، وَالْحُزْنِ بِوِلَادَتِي الْمَوْلُودَ مِنْ غَيْرِ بَعْل ﴿وَكُنْتُ نَسْيًا مَنْسِيًّا﴾ نُسِيَ فتُرِك طَلَبُهُ، كخِرَق الْحَيْضِ إِذَا أُلْقِيَتْ وَطُرِحَتْ لَمْ تُطْلَبْ وَلَمْ تُذْكَرْ. وَكَذَلِكَ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ نُسِيَ وَتُرِكَ فَهُوَ نَسِيّ.

وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ: ﴿وَكُنْتُ نَسْيًا مَنْسِيًّا﴾ أَيْ: شَيْئًا لَا يُعْرَفُ، وَلَا يُذْكَرُ، وَلَا يُدْرَى مَنْ أَنَا.

وَقَالَ الرَّبِيعُ بْنُ أَنَسٍ: ﴿وَكُنْتُ نَسْيًا مَنْسِيًّا﴾ وَهُوَ السَّقْطُ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ زَيْدٍ: لَمْ أَكُنْ شَيْئًا قَطُّ.

وَقَدْ قَدَّمْنَا الْأَحَادِيثَ الدَّالَّةَ عَلَى النَّهْيِ عَنْ تَمَنِّي الْمَوْتِ إِلَّا عِنْدَ الْفِتْنَةِ، عِنْدَ قَوْلِهِ: ﴿تَوَفَّنِي مُسْلِمًا وَأَلْحِقْنِي بِالصَّالِحِينَ﴾ [يُوسُفَ: ١٠١]

---

## 19:24-26 — verses 24-26 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Some of them read {man tahtaha} meaning "the one who was beneath her." Others read {min tahtiha} taking it as a preposition.

The commentators differed about who was meant by this. Al-Awfi and others said, from Ibn Abbas: {so he called to her from beneath her} refers to Gabriel, and Jesus did not speak until she brought him to her people. Sa'id ibn Jubayr, al-Dahhak, Amr ibn Maymun, al-Suddi, and Qatadah said likewise: it was the angel Gabriel (peace be upon him), meaning he called to her from the lower part of the valley.

Mujahid said: {so he called to her from beneath her} means Jesus son of Mary. Abd al-Razzaq said likewise, from Ma'mar, from Qatadah, who said: al-Hasan said, it is her son. This is one of the two reports from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, that it is her son; he said, have you not heard God say: {so she pointed to him} [Maryam: 29]? Ibn Zayd chose this, as did Ibn Jarir in his tafsir.

As for His saying: {do not grieve}, meaning he called out to her saying, do not grieve, {your Lord has placed beneath you a sariyy}. Sufyan al-Thawri and Shu'bah said, from Abu Ishaq, from al-Bara ibn Azib: {your Lord has placed beneath you a sariyy}, he said: it is the streamlet (al-jadwal). Ali ibn Abi Talhah said likewise, from Ibn Abbas: al-sariyy is the river. Amr ibn Maymun said the same: a river from which you may drink.

Mujahid said: it is "the river" in Syriac.

Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: al-sariyy is the small river in Nabataean.

Al-Dahhak said: it is the small river in Syriac.

Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said: it is the small river.

Qatadah said: it is al-jadwal in the language of the people of the Hijaz.

Wahb ibn Munabbih said: al-sariyy is the spring source of water.

Al-Suddi said: it is the river, and Ibn Jarir chose this view. A raised (marfu') hadith has come regarding this. Al-Tabarani said:

[chain] Abu Shu'ayb al-Harrani told us, Yahya ibn Abd Allah al-Babalutti told us, Ayyub ibn Nahik told us, I heard Ikrimah the client of Ibn Abbas say, I heard Ibn Umar say, I heard the Messenger of God ﷺ say: "The sariyy that God mentioned to Mary when He said {your Lord has placed beneath you a sariyy} is a river that God brought forth for her to drink from." This is a hadith that is extremely gharib (singular) by this route. This Ayyub ibn Nahik is al-Hubuli, of whom Abu Hatim al-Razi said: weak. Abu Zur'ah said: his hadith is munkar (rejected). Abu al-Fath al-Azdi said: his hadith is to be abandoned.

Others said: what is meant by al-sariyy is Jesus (peace be upon him). Al-Hasan, al-Rabi ibn Anas, and Muhammad ibn Abbad ibn Ja'far said this. This is one of the two reports from Qatadah, and the view of Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam. The first view is more apparent, and this is why He said afterward: {and shake toward you the trunk of the palm tree}, meaning, take hold of the trunk of the palm tree and shake it toward yourself. It is said that it was dry, as Ibn Abbas said. It is also said that it was fruit-bearing. Mujahid said: it was an ajwah (a type of date palm). Al-Thawri said, from Abu Dawud Nufay' al-A'ma: it was a sarafanah (another variety of date palm).

The apparent meaning is that it was a tree, but it was not in its season of fruiting, as Wahb ibn Munabbih said. This is why God bestowed favor upon her in this, by placing food and drink near her, saying: {it will drop upon you ripe, fresh dates, so eat and drink and let your eye be comforted}, meaning, let your soul be at ease. This is why Amr ibn Maymun said: there is nothing better for a woman in childbirth than dried and fresh dates, then he recited this noble verse.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Ali ibn al-Husayn told us, Shayban told us, Masrur ibn Sa'id al-Tamimi told us, Abd al-Rahman ibn Amr al-Awza'i told us, from Urwah ibn Ruwaym, from Ali ibn Abi Talib, who said: the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "Honor your paternal aunt, the date palm, for it was created from the same clay from which Adam (peace be upon him) was created, and there is no tree among the trees that is pollinated except it." The Messenger of God ﷺ also said: "Feed your women in childbirth fresh dates, and if there are no fresh dates then dried dates, and there is no tree more honored before God than the tree beneath which Mary daughter of Imran took shelter."

This is a hadith that is extremely munkar (rejected). Abu Ya'la related it, from Shayban, with the same chain.

Some of them read His saying "tassaqat" with doubling of the sin, and others read it without doubling. Abu Nahik read {tusaqit alayki rutaban janiyya}. Abu Ishaq related from al-Bara that he read it as "tusaqit," meaning the trunk (of the palm). All these readings are close in meaning.

As for His saying: {and if you see any human being}, meaning, whatever person you may see, {then say, I have vowed a fast to the Merciful, so I will not speak to any human today}. What is meant by "say" here is that she should indicate this to him by gesture, not that she should utter it in speech, so that it would not contradict {so I will not speak to any human today}.
